Proof for the Possibility of Resurrection
Rational and scriptural proofs for resurrection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and scriptural proofs for the permissibility of bodily resurrection after death.

Core Idea
If God created once, recreating is even easier; Scripture confirms with vivid analogies.

This lesson examines a classic argument for the possibility of resurrection. The author presents a rational proof based on God's initial creation and then reinforces it with two Quranic verses. By the end, you will see how both reason and revelation affirm that God can indeed bring the dead back to life.

Guided Path
1
Understand the question posed
Read the opening question: 'What is the proof for the permissibility of recreating creation?' This sets up the challenge that resurrection seems impossible.
The question reflects a common doubt among skeptics.
2
Study the rational proof
The author argues: God created the first creation without a prior model. If He could do that, then recreating is not beyond His power. This is a logical inference from what He has already done.
3
Analyze the first Quranic example
Read Quran 36:78-79. God responds to the one who doubts by saying that He who created the first time can create again. The first creation is a direct precedent.
This verse addresses the specific doubt about decayed bones.
4
Analyze the second Quranic example
Read Quran 36:80. God brings fire from green wood – an apparent contradiction. This illustrates God's power to produce opposite effects from opposite causes, similar to giving life to dead bones.
The analogy shows that God can create life where we see only decay.
5
Reflect on the combined argument
The rational proof establishes a general principle; the Quranic examples provide concrete parallels. Together they make a powerful case for resurrection.
Both reason and revelation agree on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : القدرة على الإيجاد والإعادة. فإن قال قائل : ما الدليل على جواز إعادة الخلق؟ قيل : الدليل على ذلك أن الله سبحانه خلقه أولاً لا على مثال سبق، فإذا خلقه أولاً لم يعيه أن يخلقه خلقاً آخر. وقد قال الله تعالى: {وَضَرَبَ لَنَا مَثَلًا وَنَسِيَ خَلْقَهُ قَالَ مَنْ يُحْيِي الْعِظَامَ وَهِيَ رَمِيمٌ قُلْ يُحْيِيهَا الَّذِي أَنْشَأَهَا أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ وَهُوَ بِكُلِّ خَلْقٍ عَلِيمٌ} [يس:78-79] فجعل النشأة الأولى دليلاً على جواز النشأة الآخرة؛ لأنها في معناها. ثم قال: {الَّذِي جَعَلَ لَكُمْ مِنَ الشَّجَرِ الْأَخْضَرِ نَارًا فَإِذَا أَنْتُمْ مِنْهُ تُوقِدُونَ} [يس:80] فجعل ظهور النار على حرها ويبسها من الشجر الأخضر على نداوته ورطوبته دليلاً على جواز خلقه الحياة في الرمة.
Issue: [God's] power over origination and re-creation. If someone says: What is the proof for the permissibility of recreating creation? It is said: The proof for that is that God, glorified, created it first without a preceding example. So if He created it first, it does not incapacitate Him to create it another creation. And God, exalted, said: 'And he strikes for Us an example and forgets his own creation. He says: "Who will give life to bones when they are decayed?" Say: "He will give them life who produced them the first time, and He is, of all creation, Knowing."' [Quran 36:78-79] So He made the first creation a proof for the permissibility of the final creation because they are similar in meaning. Then He said: '[He] who made for you from the green tree fire, and then from you ignite.' [Quran 36:80] So He made the appearance of fire, with its heat and dryness, from the green tree, despite its moisture and wetness, a proof for the permissibility of His creating life in decayed bones.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a question-and-answer format defending the possibility of bodily resurrection. The rational proof states that since God created the first creation without a preexisting model, recreating it is not beyond His power. Then two Quranic verses are cited: (1) The questioner in Surah Ya-Sin doubts resurrection of decayed bones; God responds that He who created the first time can certainly do it again. The first creation is evidence for the second because they are comparable. (2) The production of fire from green wood—an apparent contradiction (dry fire from wet wood)—is an analogy for creating life from dead bones, showing God's power to bring opposites from opposites.

Key Terms
إعادة الخلق
نشأة أولى
نشأة آخرة
رميم
شجر أخضر
نار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Recreating decayed bones is impossible because they are completely decomposed.
Correction: The source argues that God's power is not limited by physical conditions; He created the first time from nothing, so recreating from decomposed matter is easier. The Quranic analogy of fire from green wood further shows that God can produce life from its apparent opposite.

Checkpoint
What Quranic example does the author use to demonstrate the possibility of resurrection?
A) Creating the heavens and earth
B) Bringing fire out of green wood
C) The splitting of the moon
D) The story of Abraham and the birds

Key Takeaway
God's power to create the first time and the Quranic analogies prove that resurrection is not only possible but easy for Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own body and know it will one day decay, do you truly believe that the One who created you from nothing can raise you again? What doubt about God's power lingers in your heart, and how does this lesson confront it?
?
The fire from green wood shows God bringing opposites together. What 'dead' areas of your life—relationships, hopes, or faith—do you need to trust God to resurrect? What specific step will you take this week to act on that trust?
?
The skeptic in the verse forgot his own creation. In what ways do you forget your own origin and dependence on God when you face life's difficulties? How can you remind yourself daily of His power to create and re-create?

Proof of God's Omniscience from Created Order
Ash'ari argues for God's omniscience through design.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari uses the teleological argument to prove that God is omniscient, based on the intricate design of creation.

Core Idea
The precise order in creation demands a Creator who knows every detail.

This lesson presents one of the classical kalam proofs for divine omniscience. Imam al-Ash'ari begins by addressing a hypothetical question: why do you say God is knowing? He then constructs a logical argument based on the observable harmony and wisdom in the human body and the cosmos. By examining this reasoning, you will see how the order we witness points directly to the knowledge of the Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation to understand the flow of the argument.
2
Identify the key analogy
Notice the analogy of weaving brocade with images. How does this analogy establish the principle that orderly craftsmanship requires knowledge?
The analogy is central to the argument.
3
Trace the application to creation
See how Ash'ari applies the principle to the human body (life, senses, digestion) and the celestial sphere (sun, moon, stars). What do these examples show about the Creator?
4
Understand the reductio ad absurdum
Consider the hypothetical: if wise works could come from an ignorant source, then animal behaviors might be without knowledge. Why is this impossible, and how does it reinforce the conclusion?
This strengthens the logical necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إثبات كونه تعالى عالمًا
مسألة
فإن قال قائل: لم قلتم: إن الله تعالى عالم؟
قيل له: لأن الأفعال المحكمة لا تتسق في الحكمة إلا من عالم؛ وذلك أنه لا يجوز أن يحوك الديباج بالتصاوير، ويصنع دقائق الصناعة، من لا يحسن ذلك ولا يعلمه.
فلما رأينا الإنسان على ما فيه من اتساق الحكمة، كالحياة التي ركبها الله فيه، والسمع والبصر، ومجاري الطعام والشراب، وانقسامها فيه، وما هو عليه من كماله وتمامه، والفلك وما فيه من شمسه وقمره وكواكبه، ومجاريها، دل ذلك على أن الذي صنع ما ذكرناه لم يكن ليصنعه إلا وهو عالم بكيفيته وكنهه.
ولو جاز أن تحدث الصنائع الحكيمة لا من عالم، لم ندر: لعل جميع ما يحدث من حكم الحيوان، وتدابيرهم، وصنائعهم يحدث منهم وهم غير عالمين. فلما استحال ذلك، دل على أن الصنائع المحكمة لا تحدث إلا من عالم.
Proof of His Exalted being Knowing. Question: If someone says: Why do you say that God Almighty is knowing? He is told: Because well-made actions are not consistent in wisdom except from a knower. And that is because it is not possible that one who does not master it nor know it weaves brocade with images and produces precise craftsmanship. So when we see the human being in what he has of harmonious wisdom, like the life that God composed in him, hearing, sight, passages of food and drink, their distribution in him, and what he has of perfection and completion, and the celestial sphere and what is in it of its sun, moon, stars, and their orbits, that indicates that the One who made what we mentioned would not have made it unless He is knowing of its quality and essence. And if it were permissible that wise crafts occur without a knower, we would not know: perhaps all that occurs of the wisdoms of animals, their management, and their crafts occur from them while they are not knowing. So when that is impossible, it indicates that well-made crafts only occur from a knower.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a proof for God's attribute of knowledge (ʿilm). It begins with a hypothetical objection ('why do you say God is knowing?') and then provides a rational argument. The author first states the premise: well-ordered actions cannot proceed except from a knowing agent. He illustrates this with the analogy of weaving fine brocade—impossible for someone lacking skill and knowledge. Then he applies this principle to creation: observing the intricate harmony in the human body (life, senses, digestion, and completeness) and the celestial sphere (sun, moon, stars, and their motions) shows that their Maker must have full knowledge of their nature and essence. To reinforce the argument, he uses a reductio ad absurdum: if wise works could arise from an ignorant source, then we could not be certain that any animal behaviors or constructions come from knowledge—but that is impossible. Therefore, the conclusion stands: well-made crafts only come from a knower, so God, the Creator of all, is omniscient.

Key Terms
عالم
الأفعال المحكمة
الصنائع الحكيمة
اتساق الحكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument only proves God's intelligence in design generally, not specific detailed knowledge.
Correction: Ash'ari's argument specifically shows that the Creator knows the 'quality and essence' (كيفيته وكنهه) of every detail, as seen in the perfect distribution of food and drink in the body and the precise orbits of celestial bodies.

Checkpoint
How does Ash'ari argue that God must be knowing?
A) Through scriptural proof
B) Through the intricate order in creation
C) Through consensus of scholars
D) Through innate disposition

Key Takeaway
The intricate order in creation is a direct proof that its Creator possesses complete knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof argues that a perfectly crafted object cannot come from an ignorant maker. Think of the most ordinary part of your body—your hand, your eye, your heartbeat. Have you ever truly paused to acknowledge that every detail is known by God? If you were to live today with the full conviction that He knows every cell, how would it change the way you treat your body and trust His plan for your life?
?
You believe in God's omniscience intellectually, but does your daily worry suggest you sometimes doubt that He knows your specific struggles? The same knowledge that crafted the sun and moon also encompasses your smallest fear. Will you surrender one anxiety to His knowledge right now, and refuse to take it back?
?
The source says that if wise works could come from ignorance, then even animal behaviors could be without knowledge—which is absurd. Yet, how often do you attribute the 'coincidences' in your life to mere chance rather than the design of the All-Knowing? Commit to catching yourself today whenever you say 'luck' and instead say 'Allah knew.'

Proof of Life and Power through Crafted Acts
Al-Ash'ari proves that God is living and powerful through the existence of crafted acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari uses the existence of crafted acts to rationally prove that God is both living and powerful.

Core Idea
Crafted acts require a living, powerful agent; otherwise, all agency becomes uncertain.

Before diving into the theological arguments for God's attributes, we must see how reason itself points to their necessity. Al-Ash'ari presents a crisp proof: the very existence of designed actions in the world forces us to conclude that their ultimate source must be alive and capable. This passage lays the groundwork for understanding divine attributes as rationally necessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage once
Read the Arabic aloud or silently, letting the argument unfold naturally. Don't analyze yet; just absorb the flow.
Notice the logical connectors: 'likadhalika', 'fa-law', 'fa-lamma'.
2
Identify the core claim
Find the sentence that states the main conclusion: that crafted acts indicate God is living and powerful.
3
Trace the reductio argument
Al-Ash'ari uses a 'reductio ad absurdum' (if not, then...). Follow the conditional: if crafted acts could come from a non-living, powerless being, then we couldn't distinguish real agency from mere accidents. This leads to absurdity, so the original claim must be true.
This logical move is typical in kalam.
4
Reflect on the footnote
The footnote adds nuance: basic crafted acts prove life and power; perfected ones also prove knowledge. Consider what this distinction means.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كذلك لا يجوز أن تحدثَ الصَّنَائِعُ إلا مِنْ قادِرٍ حَيٍّ ؛ لأنَّه لَوْ جَازَ حُدوتُها مِمّنْ ليسَ بقادرٍ ولا حيٍّ ، لمْ نَدْرِ : لَعَلَّ سَائِرَ ما يظهرُ مِنَ النّاسِ يظهرُ منهُم وهم عَجَزَةٌ مَوتَى فلما استَحالَ ذلك، دلت الصنائع على أن الله -تعالى- حَيٌّ قادر (۱) . (۱) فمطلق «الصنائع يدل على أن الفاعل لها حي قادر، أما الصنائع المحكمة المتقنة فتفيد ذلك، وتفيد العلم خاصة.
Likewise, it is not permissible that crafted acts occur except from a powerful, living [agent]; because if it were possible for them to occur from one who is neither powerful nor living, we would not know: perhaps all that appears from people appears from them while they are incapable and dead. So when that is impossible, the crafted acts indicate that Allah - exalted - is living and powerful. (1) (1) Absolute 'crafted acts' indicate that the agent is living and powerful. As for precise, perfected crafted acts, they indicate that and also indicate knowledge specifically.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof for two divine attributes: life (al-hayat) and power (al-qudra). Al-Ash'ari argues that observable crafted acts (al-sana'i') — that is, actions that exhibit design and purpose — cannot occur except from an agent who is both living and powerful. He supports this by a reductio ad absurdum: if it were possible for such acts to come from a non-living or powerless source, then we would have no way to distinguish genuine actions from mere accidents; we could never be certain that any observed act actually came from a capable agent. Since this uncertainty is absurd (muhal), the existence of these acts themselves proves the agent must be living and powerful. The footnote expands: even basic acts indicate life and power, while perfected acts also indicate knowledge ('ilm).

Key Terms
صنائع
قادر
حي
حياة
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The mere existence of acts does not necessitate that the agent has life and power; perhaps acts can occur randomly.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari argues that if acts could occur without life and power, we could not distinguish genuine agency from random events, making all human actions uncertain. This absurdity proves that acts require a living, powerful agent.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari, why must crafted acts (al-sana'i') come from a living, powerful agent?
A) Because the Quran explicitly states so.
B) Because if they could come from a non-living or powerless being, we could not distinguish genuine acts from chance occurrences.
C) Because only perfect beings can perform any act at all.
D) Because living beings always act with power.

Key Takeaway
The existence of crafted acts rationally proves that their ultimate agent must be living and powerful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the crafted acts in your own life—your ability to think, speak, and act intentionally—do you truly recognize that these are not from your own inherent power but from the Living, Powerful Creator? Or do you live as if your agency is self-sufficient, forgetting the epistemological collapse that would follow if God were not alive and powerful? This lesson confronts you with the logical necessity of God's life and power. Will you let your daily actions remind you of this dependence, or will you continue to take your own agency for granted? Commit right now to a specific moment today where you will pause and attribute your next intentional act to the Living, Powerful God.
?
The argument shows that without God's life and power, all agency becomes uncertain. Do you sometimes act as though your own power is absolute, as if you are the ultimate originator of your deeds? This lesson exposes that assumption as irrational. How will you change your internal dialogue to consistently acknowledge that your very ability to act is a gift from the Living, Powerful One? Write down one practical step you will take today to cultivate this awareness.
?
If crafted acts—even the simplest ones—require a living, powerful agent, then every moment of your life is a testimony to God's life and power. Have you been overlooking this constant evidence? The lesson says that if we denied this, we could never be certain of any agency. Does your heart feel the weight of that certainty? What will you do today to turn your attention to the countless crafted acts around you and use them as reminders of the Creator?

Proof that Allah is Hearing and Seeing
Al-Ash'ari provides a rational proof for God's hearing and sight based on life and absence of defects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Al-Ash'ari argues rationally that Allah must be Hearing and Seeing, based on His life and the impossibility of defects.

Core Idea
A living being without defects necessarily perceives; Allah is living and defect-free, so He is Hearing and Seeing.

How can we rationally know that Allah is Hearing and Seeing without relying solely on scripture? In this passage, Al-Ash'ari answers that question using a simple logical inference from the attribute of life and the absence of defects. Let's read his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the question-and-answer format used by Al-Ash'ari.
2
Identify the core argument
Find the conditional statement: a living being without defects perceives what is heard and seen. Then see how Al-Ash'ari applies it to Allah, who is living and free from defects.
The key terms are 'living', 'defects', and 'perception'.
3
Reflect on the rational method
Note that this proof is purely rational, not based on scripture. Al-Ash'ari relies on the logical link between defectibility and contingency.
The editor's footnote mentions that dozens of Quranic verses also support this, but Al-Ash'ari chose rational proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإنْ قالَ قائل : لِمَ قُلْتُم : إِنَّ اللَّهَ سَمِيعٌ بَصِيرٌ؟ قيل له : لأنَّ الحَيَّ إذا لم يكُنْ مَوصُوفًا بآفةٍ تَمْنَعُه (۱) من إدراكِ المسموعاتِ والمُبْصَرَاتِ إِذا وُجِدَت؛ فهو سَمِيعٌ بَصِيرٌ . فلمَّا كانَ الله - تعالى - حيًّا ، لا تجوز عليه الآفات، من الصَّمَم والعَمَى وغير ذلك ؛ إِذْ كانَتِ الآفاتُ تدلُّ عَلَى حُدوثِ مَن جَازَتْ علَيْهِ، صح أنه سَمِيعٌ بَصِيرٌ (۲) (۱) في (ل): «بأنه يمنعه». (۲) اقتصر الشيخ في هذه المسألة، والتي قبلها والتي بعدها على الاستدلال العقلي، ربما لشهرة الأدلة النقلية ؛ فتوجد عشرات الآيات في القرآن التي تثبت كون الباري -تعالى- عليم سميع بصير
If a questioner says: Why do you say that Allah is Hearing, Seeing? It is said to him: Because a living being, when it is not described with a defect that prevents it (1) from perceiving what is heard and what is seen when they exist, then it is Hearing, Seeing. So since Allah - exalted - is living, defects are not possible for Him, such as deafness, blindness, and others; because defects indicate the contingency of the one on whom they occur, it is correct that He is Hearing, Seeing. (2) (1) In [manuscript L]: 'because it prevents him'. (2) The Shaykh confined himself in this issue, and the one before it and the one after it, to rational inference, perhaps due to the fame of transmitted evidences; for there are dozens of verses in the Quran that prove that the Creator - exalted - is Knowing, Hearing, Seeing.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof for the divine attributes of hearing (sam') and sight (basar). Al-Ash'ari adopts a question-and-answer format. First, he states the question: 'Why do you say that Allah is Hearing, Seeing?' The answer: a living being that is not afflicted with a defect that prevents perception (such as deafness or blindness) will necessarily perceive when the objects of perception are present. Since Allah is living and incapable of defects (because defects indicate contingency, i.e., origination in time), He must be Hearing and Seeing. The editor's footnote notes that the Shaykh relied solely on rational proof in this and neighboring issues, likely because the scriptural evidence (tens of Quranic verses) is well-known. The argument hinges on the concepts of life (hayat), defects (afat), and the link between defectibility and contingency (huduth).

Key Terms
سميع
بصير
آفات
صمم
عمى
حدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's hearing and sight are like human senses, dependent on physical organs.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari's rational proof shows that God's hearing and sight are necessary attributes of a living being without defects, not requiring physical organs.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari's argument, why is it correct that Allah is Hearing and Seeing?
A) Because the Quran explicitly mentions it, so we must accept it by faith.
B) Because Allah is living, and defects like deafness and blindness are impossible for Him, so He must perceive what is heard and seen.
C) Because all living beings can hear and see, so God must too.
D) Because prophets reported it through miracles.

Key Takeaway
Allah is Hearing and Seeing because He is living and free from defects, and a living being without defects necessarily perceives.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if Allah hears every whispered thought and sees every hidden deed? What would you do differently today if you were absolutely certain of this fact?
?
If you knew that every defect you possess—mental, physical, or moral—is a reminder of your contingency and need for Allah, how would it change your attitude toward your shortcomings?
?
When you are alone and no human sees you, are you still as conscious of Allah's sight as you are of His hearing? Which attribute do you neglect more—and what step will you take tonight to remind yourself that He is both Hearing and Seeing?

Divine Attributes
beginner
4 min
Proof of Allah's Hearing and Seeing
Al-Ash'ari proves Allah's hearing and seeing by absence of impairments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for Allah's attributes of Hearing and Seeing based on the absence of impairments.

Core Idea
Allah's perfection means no impairments; thus He hears and sees.

Al-Ash'ari presents a concise rational argument. An objector asks why we say Allah is Hearing and Seeing. The answer uses a general principle: any living being free from defects that prevent perception is necessarily Hearing and Seeing. Since Allah is Living and beyond any imperfection, these attributes follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage once. Notice that it begins with an objection (فإن قال) and then an answer (قيل له).
This is a typical kalam format: objection then response.
2
Identify the general principle
The answer states that any living being not described with an impairment that prevents perception of sounds and sights when they exist is Hearing and Seeing. This is a rational principle based on the nature of life.
The principle does not require organs; it focuses on the absence of impediments.
3
Apply the principle to Allah
Since Allah is Living and impairments are impossible for Him (because they indicate contingency), He must be Hearing and Seeing. Understand why impairments imply contingency.
Impairments are signs of createdness, which cannot apply to the Creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإنْ قالَ قائل : لِمَ قُلْتُم : إِنَّ اللَّهَ سَمِيعٌ بَصِيرٌ؟ قيل له : لأنَّ الحَيَّ إذا لم يكُنْ مَوصُوفًا بآفةٍ تَمْنَعُه من إدراكِ المسموعاتِ والمُبْصَرَاتِ إِذا وُجِدَت؛ فهو سَمِيعٌ بَصِيرٌ . فلمَّا كانَ الله - تعالى - حيًّا ، لا تجوز عليه الآفات، من الصَّمَم والعَمَى وغير ذلك ؛ إِذْ كانَتِ الآفاتُ تدلُّ عَلَى حُدوثِ مَن جَازَتْ علَيْهِ، صح أنه سَمِيعٌ بَصِيرٌ
If someone said: 'Why do you say that Allah is Hearing (samī') and Seeing (baṣīr)?' It is said to him: 'Because the living being, if it is not described with an impairment (āfah) that prevents it from perceiving audibles and visibles when they exist, then it is Hearing and Seeing. So since Allah—Exalted is He—is Living (ḥayy), and impairments such as deafness, blindness, and others are not permissible for Him—because impairments indicate the contingency (ḥudūth) of the one in whom they occur—it is correct that He is Hearing and Seeing.'
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument proving that Allah is Hearing and Seeing. The objection asks for the reason for this belief. The answer begins with a general principle: any living being that is not afflicted by an impairment that prevents perception of sounds and sights when they exist is necessarily Hearing and Seeing. Since Allah is Living and impairments are impossible for Him—because impairments are signs of contingency (ḥudūth) in the one who has them—it follows that He is Hearing and Seeing. The argument is purely rational (ʿaqlī), relying on the absence of defects rather than scriptural citation.

Key Terms
سَمِيع
بَصِير
آفة
حَي
حُدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That divine hearing and seeing involve organs or are akin to human senses.
Correction: The argument avoids this by focusing on the absence of impediments, not on physical organs. It defines the attributes in terms of capability to perceive, not physical mechanisms.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the condition for a living being to be described as Hearing and Seeing?
A) That it possesses ears and eyes
B) That it is free from impairments that prevent perception when what is perceived exists
C) That it is a human
D) That it has knowledge of all things

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes of Hearing and Seeing are rationally proven from His perfect life and the impossibility of any impairment, without requiring physical organs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If Allah's seeing is necessary from His perfection, then He sees your secret deeds and inner thoughts. What would you change today knowing that His sight is constant and inescapable?
?
This lesson argues that Allah's hearing and seeing are proven by reason, not just scripture. Does your reliance on rational certainty about Allah's attributes deepen your trust in Him, or do you still waver? What step will you take to act on that certainty?

Proof of the Pre-Eternity of Divine Attributes
Al-Ash'ari proves Allah's attributes are eternal by impossibility of their opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari uses the impossibility of opposites to prove that Allah's attributes are pre-eternal.

Core Idea
Eternal attributes are proven because their opposites are impossible for Allah.

This lesson presents a classic kalam proof for the pre-eternity of Allah's essential attributes. The argument is framed as a dialogue: an objector asks whether Allah has always been Knowing, Powerful, etc., and then demands evidence. Al-Ash'ari responds with a logical proof based on the necessary connection between life and knowledge, and the impossibility of their opposites. Let's examine this concise yet powerful reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the dialogue
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the question-and-answer format. The objector asks for affirmation and then proof.
The passage starts mid-sentence from 'فإن قال'.
2
Identify the conditional premise
Find the statement: 'if a living being is not knowing, it is described with the opposite of knowledge.' This is the key link.
3
Apply to Allah
Notice how Al-Ash'ari applies this to Allah: if He were not knowing, He would have an opposite, which is impossible.
The text ends with the conditional clause; the conclusion is implicit.
4
Understand the conclusion
Since ignorance, doubt, and impairments are impossible for Allah, He must always have been Knowing, and likewise for other attributes.
The proof extends to all essential attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإنْ قال : أتقولون: إِنَّ اللَّهَ -تعالى- لمْ يزَلْ عالمًا قادِرًا سَمِيعًا بَصِيرًا؟ قيل له : كذلك نقُولُ . فإن قال : فما الدليل على ذلك؟ قيل له : الدليل على ذلك : أن الحيَّ إذا لم يكن عالما ؛ كان موصوفًا بضد العلم من الجهل، أو الشك، أو الآفات . فلو كان الباري -تعالى- لم يزل حيًّا غير عالم ؛ لكانَ موصوفًا بضدّ العِلم ، ولو كان موصوفًا بضد العلم من الجهل أو الشك أو الآفات
If someone said: 'Do you say that Allah—Exalted is He—has always (lam yazal) been Knowing (ʿālim), Powerful (qādir), Hearing (samīʿ), Seeing (baṣīr)?' It is said to him: 'Yes, we say so.' He said: 'What is the proof of that?' It is said to him: 'The proof of that is that a living being, if it is not knowing, is described with the opposite (ḍidd) of knowledge—ignorance (jahl), doubt (shakk), or impairments (āfāt). So if the Creator—Exalted is He—had always been living but not knowing, He would be described with the opposite of knowledge; and if He were described with the opposite of knowledge—ignorance, doubt, or impairments...' (the conclusion is implied: this is impossible, so He must always be knowing).
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a question-and-answer proof for the pre-eternity (qidam) of Allah's attributes. The objector asks whether Ashʿarīs affirm that Allah has always been Knowing, Powerful, Hearing, and Seeing. The affirmative answer is given, and then the objector demands evidence. The proof uses a conditional: any living being that is not knowing is necessarily characterized by the opposite of knowledge, namely ignorance, doubt, or impairments. If Allah—who is Living and pre-eternal—were not knowing, He would have to be characterized by one of these opposites. But ignorance, doubt, and impairments are all impossible for Allah because they entail contingency (ḥudūth). Therefore, it is logically necessary that Allah has always been Knowing, and likewise for the other attributes. The argument establishes the eternity of multiple attributes by focusing on the impossibility of their contraries.

Key Terms

عالم
قادر
سَمِيع
بَصِير
ضد العلم
جهل
شك
آفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah's attributes are acquired or change over time.
Correction: This proof shows that attributes like knowledge are essential to Allah's nature and pre-eternal, because their opposites (ignorance, doubt, impairments) are impossible for Him.

Checkpoint
According to the proof in this passage, why must Allah have always been Knowing?
A) Because the Qur'an says so
B) Because if He were not knowing, He would have ignorance, which is impossible for Allah
C) Because all living beings are knowing
D) Because knowledge is a necessary attribute of life

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari proves the pre-eternity of Allah's attributes by showing that their opposites are impossible for the perfect Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that Allah is eternally Knowing — He has always known you, including your darkest secrets and most shameful moments. How does knowing that His knowledge of you preceded your own existence change the way you approach repentance? Will you confess your sins honestly, knowing He already knows them perfectly?
?
The proof says ignorance is impossible for Allah. So when you face a situation that feels confusing or unfair, do you truly believe that Allah's knowledge encompasses its wisdom? Or do you secretly doubt that He knows what’s best? Commit today to surrender that doubt.
?
If Allah’s power is eternal and unchanging, then no difficulty you face is beyond His ability. Is there an area of your life where you have been acting as if Allah is weak or unaware? What specific step will you take this week to trust in His power over that situation?

Proof of the Eternality of Allah's Attributes
Imam Ash'ari proves the eternality of Allah's knowledge, power, hearing, and sight via the impossibility of change from an eternal opposite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Ash'ari's argument that Allah's attributes of knowledge, power, hearing, and sight are eternal, based on the impossibility of an eternal opposite ceasing to exist.

Core Idea
Allah's eternal attributes are proven by the impossibility of an eternal opposite ceasing to exist.

Imam Ash'ari addresses a fundamental question: Has Allah always possessed His attributes? In this passage, he presents a logical proof rooted in the nature of opposites. The argument shows that if Allah were not eternally knowing, then ignorance would be eternal, and eternal ignorance cannot be removed. Yet the wise works of creation indicate knowledge, so knowledge must be eternal. The same reasoning applies to power, hearing, and sight.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the objection
The objector asks whether Allah has always been knowing, powerful, hearing, seeing. Notice the format: 'If he says...' followed by the answer.
The objection sets up the proof.
2
Follow the proof for knowledge
The argument uses the concept of 'opposite' (ضد). If Allah were not knowing, He would be described with the opposite of knowledge (ignorance, doubt, defects). If that opposite were eternal, it could not cease, making it impossible for Allah to ever become knowing. But He has performed wise works, proving He is knowing. Therefore, He must have always been knowing.
This is the most detailed argument.
3
See the parallel reasoning for power
The same logic: if not powerful, then weakness would be eternal, and actions could not come from Him. Yet actions exist, so He must be eternally powerful.
4
Understand the proof for hearing and sight
If not hearing and seeing, then deafness and blindness would be eternal. But defects like these are impossible for the Creator because they are signs of temporality. Therefore, He must have always been hearing and seeing.
This argument adds the impossibility of defects on the Creator.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends by stating that what has been said indicates that Allah has always been knowing, powerful, hearing, seeing. Notice how the proof does not rely on scripture alone but on rational necessity.
This is a standard kalam argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال : أتقولونَ: إِنَّ اللَّهَ -تعالى- لمْ يَزَلْ عالمًا قادِرًا سَمِيعًا بَصِيرًا؟ قيل له : كذلك نقُولُ . فإن قال : فما الدليل على ذلك؟ قيل له : الدليل على ذلك : أن الحيَّ إذا لم يكن عالما ؛ كان موصوفًا بضد العلم من الجهل، أو الشك، أو الآفات . فلو كان [الكباري -تعالى- لم يزل حيًّا غير عالم ؛ لكانَ موصوفا بضدّ العِلم ، ( ولو كان موصوفًا بضد العلم من الجهل أو الشك أو الآفات). ولو كان لم يزل موصوفًا بضدّ العِلم، لاستحالَ أنْ يَعْلَمَ ؛ لأنَّ ضِدَّ العلمِ لَوْ كانَ قديما ؛ لاسْتَحالَ أنْ يَبْطل، وإذا استحال أن يَبْطَلَ ذلك لَمْ يجُزْ أن يصنعَ الصنائعَ الحِكْميَّة، فلما صنعها ودلت على أنه عالم ، صَحَ وثَبَتَ أنه لم يزل عالما ؛ إِذْ قدِ اسْتَحالَ أنْ يكونَ لم يزل بضدّ العِلمِ موصوفا. [إثبات القدرة] وكذلك لو كان لم يزل حيًّا غير قادِر ؛ لوجب أن يكون لم يزل عاجزا موصوفًا بِضِدّ القُدرةِ، ولو كان عجزُهُ قديما ، لاسْتَحَالَ أنْ يَقْدِرَ وأن تحدثَ الأفعالُ منه . [إثبات قدم السمع والبصر] وكذلك لوْ كانَ لم يزل حيًّا غيرَ سَمِيعِ ولَا بَصِيرٍ، لكانَ لَمْ يَزَلْ مَوْصوفًا بضدّ السمع مِنَ الصَّمَم والآفاتِ، وبضدِّ البَصَرِ مِنَ العَمَى والآفاتِ، ومُحالٌ جَوازُ الآفات على الباري؛ لأنَّها مِنْ سِماتِ الحَدَثِ، فَدَلَّ ما قُلْناهُ على أنَّ اللَّهَ -تعالى- لَمْ يَزَلْ عالمًا قادرًا سميعا بصيرًا
If he says: Do you say that Allah, exalted, has always been knowing, powerful, hearing, seeing? It is said to him: Thus we say. If he says: What is the proof of that? It is said to him: The proof of that is that the living being, if it is not knowing, is described with the opposite of knowledge: ignorance, or doubt, or defects. For if [the Creator] - exalted - had always been living, not knowing, He would be described with the opposite of knowledge (and He would be described with the opposite of knowledge: ignorance, or doubt, or defects). And if He had always been described with the opposite of knowledge, it would be impossible for Him to know; because if the opposite of knowledge were eternal, it would be impossible for it to cease. And if it is impossible for that to cease, it is not permissible for Him to perform wise works. So when He performed them and they indicated that He is knowing, it became correct and established that He has always been knowing, since it is impossible that He had always been described with the opposite of knowledge. [Proof of power] Similarly, if He had always been living, not powerful, then it would be necessary that He had always been weak, described with the opposite of power. And if His weakness were eternal, it would be impossible for Him to be powerful and for actions to come from Him. [Proof of the eternality of hearing and sight] Similarly, if He had always been living, not hearing nor seeing, He would have always been described with the opposite of hearing: deafness and defects, and with the opposite of sight: blindness and defects. And the occurrence of defects upon the Creator is impossible, because they are signs of temporality. So what we have said indicates that Allah, exalted, has always been knowing, powerful, hearing, seeing.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the eternality of Allah's attributes of knowledge, power, hearing, and sight. It is structured as an objection-and-answer followed by three parallel arguments. First, the objector asks whether Allah has always been knowing, powerful, hearing, and seeing. The answer is yes. Then the proof is requested. The imam provides a common argument: if a living being is not knowing, it must be described with the opposite of knowledge (ignorance, doubt, defects). If Allah had always been living but not knowing, then that opposite of knowledge would be eternal. Since an eternal opposite cannot cease to exist, it would be impossible for Allah to ever become knowing. However, Allah has created wise works (the universe and its order) which indicate knowledge. Therefore, He must have always been knowing, because if He had been described with the opposite eternally, He could not later acquire knowledge. The same reasoning applies to power: if He were not always powerful, He would be eternally weak, and weakness cannot turn into power, yet actions occur from Him, so He must be eternally powerful. Similarly for hearing and sight: if not eternally hearing and seeing, He would be eternally deaf and blind, but defects like deafness and blindness are impossible for the Creator because they are signs of temporality. Thus, the existence of perfect actions and the impossibility of defects prove that Allah has always been knowing, powerful, hearing, and seeing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof relies on the idea that God cannot change at all.
Correction: The argument is specifically about the impossibility of an eternal opposite ceasing to exist, not a blanket statement that God cannot change. Change is possible for temporal attributes, but an eternal opposite cannot be removed.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Ash'ari, why must Allah have always been knowing?
A) Because His actions are wise, which requires knowledge, and if He were not knowing, He would be eternally ignorant, which could not change.
B) Because the Quran says so.
C) Because all beings need knowledge.
D) Because knowledge is a necessary attribute of life.

Key Takeaway
The existence of wise actions and the impossibility of defects prove that Allah has always been knowing, powerful, hearing, and seeing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah had not always been knowing, you would have no certainty that His knowledge is perfect now. What would that mean for your trust in His promises and warnings? Will you commit today to relying on His eternal knowledge for every decision you face?
?
The proof shows that an eternal opposite (like ignorance) would make it impossible for Allah to ever become knowing. Are there any 'eternal opposites' in your own life—habits or beliefs you have held so long that you think you cannot change? What would it take for you to break them, knowing that Allah's power enables change?
?
Imam Ash'ari argues that wise works point to an eternally wise Creator. Look at your own actions—do they reflect the wisdom of the One you worship? What is one area of your life where your actions do not align with acknowledging Allah's perfect knowledge and power, and how will you adjust it starting today?

Proof of God's Eternal Attributes: Knowledge, Power, Hearing, Sight
Ashari proves God's eternal knowledge, power, hearing, and sight through the impossibility of opposite attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that God's attributes of knowledge, power, hearing, and sight are eternal and cannot have been acquired.

Core Idea
An eternal opposite cannot cease; thus God always had these attributes.

This passage from Imam al-Ash'ari presents a foundational kalam argument for the eternity of God's attributes. The proof is based on the impossibility of an eternal attribute ceasing to exist. By examining God's wise actions and the impossibility of defects, the argument demonstrates that God has always been knowing, powerful, hearing, and seeing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of the argument. Notice the repeated logical structure for each attribute.
The passage uses a conditional reasoning: if God had an opposite attribute eternally, it could never change.
2
Identify the four attributes and their opposites
The argument addresses knowledge (opposite: ignorance), power (opposite: incapability), hearing (opposite: deafness), and sight (opposite: blindness). List them and see how each is used.
3
Understand the key premise: eternal attributes cannot cease
The core premise is that if something is eternal, it cannot be removed. Therefore, if God had ignorance eternally, He could never become knowing. Grasp this before moving on.
This is the backbone of the proof.
4
See how the argument applies to each attribute
For knowledge: wise actions prove God is knowing, so He must have always been knowing. For power: actions occur from Him, so He must have always been powerful. For hearing and sight: defects are impossible for God, so He must have always been hearing and seeing.
The same logic is applied to all four.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that Allah never ceased to be knowing, powerful, hearing, and seeing. Understand that this establishes the eternity of these attributes.
This is a standard Ash'ari proof against those who claim God acquired attributes in time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كان لَمْ يزل موصوفًا بضدّ العِلم، لاستحالَ أنْ يَعْلَمَ ؛ لأنَّ ضِدَّ العلمِ لَوْ كانَ قديما لاسْتَحالَ أنْ يَبْطل، وإذا استحال أن يَبْطَلَ ذلك لَمْ يجُزْ أن يصنعَ الصنائعَ الحِكْميَّة، فلما صنعها ودلت على أنه عالم ، صَحَ وثَبَتَ أنه لم يزل عالما ؛ إِذْ قدِ اسْتَحالَ أنْ يكونَ لم يزل بضدّ العِلمِ موصوفا. وكذلك لو كان لم يزل حيًّا غير قادِر ؛ لوجب أن يكون لم يزل عاجزا موصوفًا بِضِدّ القُدرةِ، ولو كان عجزُهُ قديما ، لاسْتَحَالَ أنْ يَقْدِرَ وأن تحدثَ الأفعالُ منه. وكذلك لوْ كانَ لم يزل حيًّا غيرَ سَمِيعِ ولَا بِصِيرٍ، لكانَ لَمْ يَزَلْ السمع مَوْصوفًا بضِدّ السمع مِنَ الصَّمَم والآفاتِ، وبضدِّ البَصَرِ مِنَ العَمَى والبَصَرِ والآفاتِ، ومُحالٌ جَوازُ الآفات على الباري؛ لأنَّها مِنْ سِماتِ الحَدَثِ، فَدَلَّ ما قُلْناهُ على أنَّ اللَّهَ -تعالى- لَمْ يَزَلْ عالمًا قادرًا سميعا بصيرًا
And if He had never ceased to be described with the opposite of knowledge, it would be impossible for Him to know; because if the opposite of knowledge were eternal, it would be impossible for it to cease. And if it is impossible for that to cease, it would not be permissible for Him to perform wise actions. And when He performed them and they indicated that He is knowing, it became correct and established that He never ceased to be knowing, since it is impossible that He never ceased to be described with the opposite of knowledge. And likewise, if He had never ceased to be living but not powerful, then it would be necessary that He never ceased to be described with the opposite of power, i.e., incapable. And if His incapability were eternal, it would be impossible for Him to be powerful and for actions to occur from Him. And likewise, if He had never ceased to be living but not hearing and not seeing, then He would never cease to be described with the opposite of hearing, i.e., deafness and defects, and with the opposite of sight, i.e., blindness and defects. And it is impossible for defects to befall the Creator, because they are marks of originatedness. So what we have said indicates that Allah, exalted, never ceased to be knowing, powerful, hearing, seeing.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the eternity of four of God's attributes: knowledge, power, hearing, and sight. The author uses the principle of the impossibility of transition from an eternal opposite. The argument proceeds in four parallel steps. First, regarding knowledge: if God were eternally described with ignorance (the opposite of knowledge), it would be impossible for Him to ever become knowledeable, because an eternal attribute cannot cease. But we observe that God performs wise actions (like creation), which indicate knowledge. Therefore, He must have been knowing eternally; otherwise, the impossibility argument would hold. Second, regarding power: if God were eternally powerless (incapable), He could never become powerful or produce actions. But actions do occur from Him, so He must be eternally powerful. Third, regarding hearing and sight: if God were eternally without hearing and sight, He would be described with their opposites (deafness, blindness, etc.). But such defects are impossible for the Creator, as they are signs of originatedness (contingency). Therefore, He must be eternally hearing and seeing. The conclusion unites all four attributes: God is eternally knowing, powerful, hearing, and seeing.

Key Terms
ضدّ العلم
ضدّ القدرة
ضدّ السمع
الصنائع الحكمية
سمات الحدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God acquired knowledge or power at some point in time after not having them.
Correction: The argument shows that if the opposite of an attribute were eternal, it could never cease, so God must have always had the attribute. Wise actions and the impossibility of defects confirm that God never lacked these attributes.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it impossible for God to have had no power (being incapable) at first and then later become powerful?
A) Because incapability is a defect and defects cannot befall God.
B) Because if incapability were eternal, it could never cease, so He could never become powerful.
C) Because the Quran says God is all-powerful.
D) Because wise actions require power from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
God's attributes of knowledge, power, hearing, and sight are proven eternal by the impossibility of their opposites being eternal and then ceasing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that Allah's knowledge of you is eternal and encompasses every action you will ever commit, would you live differently today? What would you change in your daily choices to align with that reality?
?
The proof shows that Allah cannot have defects like deafness or blindness because they are marks of createdness. Are you willing to examine your own mental image of Allah and consciously remove any human-like imperfections you might unconsciously attribute to Him? What would that require of you?
?
The argument uses the impossibility of opposites: an eternal state cannot cease. Is there an area of your life where you are trying to combine opposites—such as claiming to rely on Allah's eternal power while acting as if your own efforts are the ultimate cause? What would it mean to fully surrender that area to Allah's sole control?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
5 min
Proof that God Possesses Knowledge
Ashari defends that God has a real attribute of knowledge, not just being described as knowing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ashari argues that God's attribute of knowledge is inseparable from His being described as knowing, based on the analogy from human actions.

Core Idea
The same proof that God is knowing also proves He has knowledge.

In this passage, Ashari responds to an objector who questions why we affirm a distinct attribute of knowledge for God. The reply hinges on logical parity: if wise actions indicate both that humans are knowing and have knowledge, then for God the same actions must indicate both. Denying one while affirming the other would destroy the analogy and lead to absurdity. This lesson unpacks that argument and shows why the Islamic theological tradition insists on real divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the objection-and-answer format.
The passage uses a rhetorical question and a direct response.
2
Identify the core analogy
Recognize that Ashari builds an analogy between human wise actions and God's wise actions. For humans, such actions indicate both that the agent is knowing (عالم) and that he has knowledge (علم).
This analogy is a standard kalam methodology: qiyas al-gha'ib 'ala al-shahid.
3
Understand the reduction to absurdity
Ashari shows that if you accept the analogy for 'knowing' but reject it for 'knowledge', the reasoning becomes inconsistent: one could then claim actions indicate our knowledge but not that we are knowing.
This logical move forces the objector to either accept both or reject both.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that God must have a real attribute of knowledge; otherwise, the entire analogical proof for God being knowing collapses.
This defends the Ash'ari position of affirming real, distinct attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : لمَ قلتُم إِنَّ لِلْبَارِي -تعالى- عِلمًا بِهِ عَلِمَ؟ قيل له : لأنَّ الصنائعَ الحِكميَّةَ، كما لا تقع منا إلا من عالم، كذلك لا تحدثُ مِنَّا إِلا مِنْ ذِي عِلْمٍ، فلو لم تدلَّ الصنائع على عِلْمٍ مَن ظهرتْ مِنهُ منَّا ، لم تدلَّ على أن مَنْ ظهرت منه منا فهو عالِمٌ . فلو دلَّتْ على أن الباري - تعالى - عالم؛ قياسًا على دلالتها على أنَّا علماءُ ، ولم تدل على أن له علما؛ قياسًا على دلالتها على أن لنا علما ، لجازَ لزاعم أنْ يزعم أنها تدلُّ على عِلْمِنا ولا تدلّ على أنَّا عُلَماءُ. وإذا لم يَجُز هذا لم يَجُز ما قاله هَذا القائل.
If someone says: Why do you say that the Creator, exalted, has knowledge by which He knows? It is said to him: Because wise actions, just as they do not occur from us except from one who is knowing, likewise they do not occur from us except from one who possesses knowledge. So if the actions did not indicate knowledge in the one from whom they appear in us, they would not indicate that the one from whom they appear in us is knowing. So if they indicate that the Creator, exalted, is knowing, by analogy to their indication that we are knowing, but they do not indicate that He has knowledge, by analogy to their indication that we have knowledge, then it would be permissible for a claimant to claim that they indicate our knowledge but do not indicate that we are knowledgeable. And if this is not permissible, then what this speaker said is not permissible.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer defending the existence of knowledge as an attribute of God (not just the description 'knowing'). The objector asks: why do you affirm that God has a distinct attribute called 'knowledge'? The answer uses an analogy (qiyas al-gha'ib 'ala al-shahid) from human experience. We observe that wise actions from humans indicate two things: that the agent is knowing (عالم) and that the agent possesses knowledge (علم). If we deny the latter for God, the analogy breaks down. Specifically: if wise actions indicate only that the agent is knowing but not that he has knowledge, then by the same logic they could indicate that we have knowledge but not that we are knowing. But that is absurd. Therefore, since the actions indicate both for humans, they must indicate both for God. The author's point is that the inference from actions to 'being knowing' and 'having knowledge' is inseparable; you cannot accept one and reject the other without inconsistency.

Key Terms
صنائع حكمية
قياس الغائب على الشاهد
عالم
علم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is sufficient to say God is knowing without affirming a distinct attribute of knowledge.
Correction: The argument shows that the same evidence that proves God is knowing also proves He has knowledge; separating them would make the evidence inconsistent.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the argument in this passage?
A) That God's knowledge is unlike human knowledge.
B) That if wise actions from humans indicate both that they are knowing and that they have knowledge, then for God the same actions must indicate both.
C) That humans can know God through actions.
D) That God's knowledge is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The very same evidence that proves God is knowing necessarily proves He has knowledge; to affirm one without the other is incoherent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself content with saying 'Allah knows' without truly reflecting that His knowledge is a real, distinct attribute that underlies His perfect judgment? How would your trust in His decress deepen if you pondered that His knowledge is not just a description but a reality in His essence?
?
The argument shows that separating 'knowing' from 'knowledge' leads to absurdity. In your own life, do you sometimes separate your beliefs from actions—claiming to know something but living as if you don't? How does this lesson challenge you to integrate your knowledge of God into your daily decisions?

Proving Allah's Knowledge Through the Analogy of Wise Acts
Imam Ashari proves divine knowledge via analogy of wise acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ashari uses the analogy from human experience to prove that Allah has an attribute of knowledge, and how he defends the necessary correlation between being a knower and having knowledge.

Core Idea
Wise acts always come from a knower with knowledge—so must the Creator's.

This lesson presents a classic theological proof from Imam Ashari. He argues that the wise, orderly acts in creation are analogous to deliberate human acts—they require both a knowing agent and the attribute of knowledge. Through this analogy, he establishes that Allah has an eternal attribute of knowledge. The passage also addresses a potential objection about the relationship between 'knower' and 'knowledge'.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping, then read the translation. Notice the question-and-answer structure.
Pay attention to the flow: question, answer, objection, counter-argument.
2
Identify the core analogy
Find where the analogy is drawn between human acts and divine acts. The key phrase is 'الصنائع الحكمية' (wise acts).
The analogy is based on our common experience: wise acts only come from someone who is knowing and has knowledge.
3
Examine the objection and response
Read the opponent's objection: that being a knower might not necessarily imply having knowledge. Then see Imam Ashari's two responses: a symmetrical argument and a definitional argument.
The definitional response is crucial: 'knower' means 'one who has knowledge'.
4
Grasp the necessary correlation
Understand that for Imam Ashari, 'knower' and 'knowledge' are inseparable. You cannot have one without the other, just as you cannot have a speaker without speech.
This is the foundation of the proof for divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٩] مسألة فإن قال قائل : لمَ قلتُم إِنَّ لِلْبَارِي -تعالى- عِلمًا بِهِ عَلِمَ؟ قيل له : لأنَّ الصنائعَ الحِكميَّةَ ، كما لا تقع منا إلا من عالم، كذلك لا تحدثُ مِنَّا إِلا مِنْ ذِي عِلْمٍ، فلو لم تدلَّ الصنائع على عِلْمٍ مَن ظهرتْ مِنهُ منَّا ، لم تدلَّ على أن مَنْ ظهرت منه منا فهو عالِمٌ . فلو دلَّتْ على أن الباري - تعالى - عالم؛ قياسًا على دلالتها على أنَّا علماءُ ، ولم تدل على أن له علما؛ قياسًا على دلالتها على أن لنا علما ، لجازَ لزاعم أنْ يزعم أنها تدلُّ على عِلْمِنا ولا تدلّ على أنَّا عُلَماءُ. وإذا لم يَجُز هذا لم يَجُز ما قاله هَذا القائل .
فإن قال : فما أنكرتم أن لا تدل الأفعال الحكمية على علم العالم منا كما دلت على أنه عالم؟ لأنه ليس معنى العالم منا أن له علما ؛ لأنه قدْ يَعْلَمُ العالَمَ مِنَّا عَالِمًا مَنْ لا يعلم أن له علما ؟ قيل له : إن جاز لك أن تزعَمَ هذا جاز لغيرِكَ أن يزعم أن الأفعال الحكمية تدلُّ على أن لي علما بها ، ولا تدل على أني عالم ؛ لأنه ليس معنى العالم أن له علما ؛ لأنَّه قد يَعْلَمُ الإِنسانَ منا أنّ له علمًا مَنْ لا يَعْلَمُهُ عَالِمًا، وأيضًا النَّاسِي . وأيضًا هذه الدعوى - عندي - فاسدة؛ وذلك أن معنى العالم عندي أن له علما ، ومَنْ لم يعلم لزيدٍ عِلما لم يعلمه عالِمًا .
[9] Issue: If someone says: Why do you say that the Creator - exalted - has knowledge by which He knows? It is said to him: Because wise acts, just as they do not occur from us except from a knower, similarly they do not occur from us except from one who has knowledge. So if the acts did not indicate knowledge of the one from whom they appear from us, they would not indicate that the one from whom they appear from us is a knower. So if they indicated that the Creator - exalted - is knowing, by analogy to their indication that we are knowing, but did not indicate that He has knowledge, by analogy to their indication that we have knowledge, then it would be permissible for a claimant to claim that they indicate our knowledge but do not indicate that we are knowing. And if this is not permissible, then what this speaker said is not permissible. Then he said: What is your objection to the fact that wise acts do not indicate the knowledge of the knower from us, just as they indicate that he is knowing? Because the meaning of 'knower' from us is not that he has knowledge, because sometimes someone may know a knower from us who does not know that he has knowledge. It is said to him: If it is permissible for you to claim this, it would be permissible for another to claim that wise acts indicate that I have knowledge by them, but do not indicate that I am knowing, because the meaning of 'knower' is not that he has knowledge, because sometimes someone may know that a person has knowledge who does not know him as knowing, and also the forgetful person. And also this claim - in my view - is invalid; because the meaning of 'knower' in my view is that he has knowledge, and whoever does not know that Zaid has knowledge does not know him as knowing.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a structured theological argument (mas'ala) in which Imam Ashari proves that Allah has an attribute of knowledge (علم) using the method of analogy from the witnessed (قياس الغائب على الشاهد). The argument proceeds as follows: First, a questioner asks why the Ash'aris affirm that Allah has knowledge by which He knows. The answer draws an analogy from human experience: just as wise, skilful acts (الصنائع الحكمية) in humans only occur from a knower (عالم) and only from one who has knowledge (ذو علم), so too the wise acts of creation indicate that the Creator is both knowing and has knowledge. The proof is based on the inseparable correlation between being a knower and having knowledge. If one were to accept that the acts indicate that we are knowing but not that we have knowledge, then by the same logic one could claim that they indicate our knowledge but not that we are knowing—an absurd contradiction. The opponent then raises an objection: perhaps the acts indicate that a human is a knower but not that he has knowledge, since one might recognize a person as a knower without knowing that he has knowledge (e.g., a forgetful person who appears knowledgeable). The Imam refutes this in two ways. First, by symmetrical argument: if that were permissible, then one could also claim the opposite—that acts indicate knowledge but not the knower. Second, by defining the term: the true meaning of 'knower' (عالم) is precisely 'one who has knowledge' (له علم). Therefore, knowing someone as a knower necessarily entails knowing that he has knowledge. The argument establishes that Allah necessarily has an attribute of knowledge, which is eternal and distinct from His essence.

Key Terms
علم
عالم
صنائع حكمية
قياس الغائب على الشاهد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the argument is circular because it assumes knowledge from the attribute of being a knower.
Correction: Imam Ashari clarifies that the two are necessarily correlative—one cannot have a knower without knowledge. The argument is not circular but based on the definitional inseparability.

Checkpoint

A) Because the Qur'an explicitly states it.
B) Because wise acts require a knower with knowledge, and this is established by analogy from human experience.
C) Because knowledge is an eternal attribute that cannot be denied.
D) Because all prophets reported that Allah has knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Imam Ashari proves Allah's knowledge by showing that wise acts require a knower who has knowledge, and the same applies to the Creator.

Defining Otherness and Its Implication for Divine Attributes
Al-Ash'ari defines otherness as possible separation and proves God's knowledge is not other than His essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's definition of 'otherness' as possible separation and why it implies that God's attributes are not distinct from His essence.

Core Idea
Otherness means possible separation; God and His attributes cannot separate, so they are not other.

In this passage, al-Ash'ari responds to an objection that the act of wisdom indicating knowledge implies that knowledge is other than the knower. He clarifies the precise meaning of 'otherness' and then applies it to the divine attributes, showing that God's knowledge is not other than His essence because both are eternal and cannot separate.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the passage carefully, noticing how al-Ash'ari first rejects an analogy, then defines otherness, and finally applies it to God.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the definition of otherness
Al-Ash'ari defines otherness as the possibility of separation. Think about what this means: two things are 'other' only if they can exist apart in some way.
3
Apply the definition to divine attributes
Since God and His knowledge are both eternal, and eternal things cannot possibly separate, they cannot be considered distinct. Grasp the logical force of this argument.
This is a key argument in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قيل له : ليسَ إذا دل الفعلُ الحكمي على أنّ للإنسانِ علما دلَّ على أنه غَيرُه ، كما ليسَ إذا دلّ على أنه عالم دلَّ على أنه متغاير على وجه من الوجوه وأيضًا فإن معنى «الغيرية» : جَوازُ مفارقة أحَدِ الشيئين للآخر على وجه من الوجوه ، فلمَّا دلتِ الدلالة على قدم الباري -تعالى- وعلمه ، استَحالَ أن يكونَا غَيْرَيْنِ .
It was said to him: If the act of wisdom indicates that a human has knowledge, it does not indicate that it is other than him, just as when it indicates that he is knowing, it does not indicate that he is distinct in any manner. And also, the meaning of 'otherness' is the possibility of one of two things separating from the other in some manner. So when the evidence indicated the eternity of the Creator—Exalted is He—and His knowledge, it became impossible for them to be two others.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof. Al-Ash'ari first responds to an opponent who claims that the act of wisdom (الفعل الحكمي) indicating knowledge implies that knowledge is something other than the knower. He argues that just as the act indicating that someone is a knower does not indicate that he is distinct in any way, similarly it does not indicate otherness. He then defines otherness (الغيرية) as the possibility of separation (جَوازُ مفارقة) between two things in some manner, whether in existence, time, or place. Since evidence has established the eternity of God and His knowledge, and eternal things cannot possibly separate from each other (as separation would imply temporal change), it follows that God and His knowledge cannot be two distinct things (غَيْرَيْنِ). Thus the divine attributes are not other than the essence.

Key Terms
الفعل الحكمي
الغيرية
جَوازُ مفارقة
قدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'otherness' simply means conceptual distinction, like a difference in definition.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari defines otherness more strongly as the possibility of separation in existence, time, or place, not mere conceptual difference.

Checkpoint

B) The possibility of separation between two things
C) Being created
D) Being independent in existence

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari defines otherness as possible separation, and because God and His attributes are eternal and cannot separate, they are not distinct or 'other'.

The Symmetrical Argument Linking Knowledge and Knower
Al-Ash'ari uses a symmetrical argument to prove that indication of the act to the knower also indicates knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari uses a symmetry argument to prove that the act of wisdom simultaneously indicates both the knower and his knowledge.

Core Idea
What indicates the knower also indicates knowledge—you cannot separate them.

Al-Ash'ari presents a clever logical move: if someone claims that the act first shows us the knower and only later his knowledge, then by symmetry someone else could claim the reverse. Both claims are equally absurd, so the only consistent position is that the act indicates both at once. This lesson walks you through that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if it were permissible... then it would be permissible...'
The argument is a reductio ad absurdum.
2
Identify the two hypothetical claims
Find the two parallel claims: (1) act indicates knower first, then knowledge; (2) act indicates knowledge first, then knower. Why are they symmetrical?
3
Understand the equivalence and conclusion
Al-Ash'ari says both are equally impermissible ('لم يجز هذا وتكافأ القولان'). Therefore, the act's indication of the knower is necessarily also an indication of knowledge.
The phrase 'تكافأ القولان' means the two statements are equivalent (in absurdity).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا : فلَوْ جَازَ لِزاعِمٍ أَنْ يَزْعُمَ أَنَّ الفعلَ الحِكْمِيَّ يَدلُّ على أنّ العالم عالم ، ثم يُعلَمُ عِلمُهُ بعد ذلك، لَجَازَ لزاعمٍ أَنْ يَرْعُمَ أَنَّ الفعل الحكمي يدلُّ على أنّ العِلْمَ عِلْمٌ ، ثم يعلم أنه لعالم بعد ذلك . وإذا لمْ يَجُز هذا وتكافأ القولان، وجب أن تكون الدلالة على أن العالِم عَالِم دلالة على العِلم .
And also: If it were permissible for a claimant to claim that the act of wisdom indicates that the knower is a knower, and then his knowledge is known after that, then it would be permissible for a claimant to claim that the act of wisdom indicates that knowledge is knowledge, and then it is known that it belongs to a knower after that. And if this is not permissible and the two statements are equivalent, then it is necessary that the indication that the knower is a knower is an indication of knowledge.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a proof by symmetry. Al-Ash'ari proposes a hypothetical: If someone claimed that the act of wisdom (الفعل الحكمي) first indicates that the knower is a knower, and only subsequently (as a separate step) that he has knowledge, then by the same logic it would be possible for someone else to claim that the act first indicates that knowledge is knowledge, and only later that it belongs to a knower. But both claims are equally impermissible (لم يجز) because the act simultaneously indicates both. Since the two scenarios are parallel and equally absurd, the correct position is that the act's indication that the knower is a knower is necessarily also an indication of the knowledge itself. Thus the knowledge is inseparably known from the act, and it is not something inferred separately.

Key Terms
الفعل الحكمي
دلالة
تكافأ القولان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the act indicates the knower first and then the knowledge is inferred separately.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows that this leads to an absurd symmetry: if one can separate, then one could also start with knowledge first. So the only consistent position is that the act indicates both simultaneously.

Checkpoint

A) The act indicates knowledge only indirectly
B) The act's indication of the knower is also an indication of knowledge
C) The act indicates neither knowledge nor the knower
D) The act indicates the knower but not the knowledge

Key Takeaway
The act of wisdom simultaneously indicates both the knower and his knowledge; you cannot separate them into two separate indications.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see wisdom in the universe, do you immediately recognize both the All-Wise and His wisdom, or do you separate them in your mind? What does this argument reveal about the intimacy of Allah's attributes with His actions?
?
If the act of wisdom simultaneously indicates the knower and his knowledge, how should this affect your awareness of Allah's presence? Are you content to see only the creation without acknowledging the Creator and His attributes together?
?
This argument shows that knowledge and knower are inseparable in indication. Is your faith in Allah's attributes also inseparable from your recognition of His acts? Or do you sometimes treat His attributes as distant concepts?

Refutation of the mortality-based objection
Al-Ash'ari refutes the mortality-based objection with a reductio argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's use of reductio ad absurdum to refute the claim that the act of wisdom indicates knowledge only because the agent is mortal.

Core Idea
If mortality explains knowledge indication, it also absurdly explains the knower.

Al-Ash'ari now tackles a subtle objection: that the act of wisdom indicates knowledge only because the agent could die and become ignorant. This would tie knowledge to contingency. He refutes it by turning the argument against itself, showing that the same logic leads to an absurd conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the first sentence carefully: what is the objector claiming? Notice the conditional reasoning: 'What prevents that... because he is one who may die and become ignorant.'
The objector is trying to restrict the evidence of the act to mortal agents.
2
Identify the refutation
Now read al-Ash'ari's reply. He uses a mirror argument: 'If this were permissible, then it would be permissible to claim...' What is that alternative claim?
3
Understand the reductio
Al-Ash'ari shows that the objector's reasoning would force an absurd implication: that the act also indicates the knower as a knower solely because of mortality. Since that is not what the act indicates, the original premise is false.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum: assume the premise, derive a contradiction, reject the premise.
4
Consider the application to God
Reflect: if mortality were the reason, then the act of wisdom from God (who never dies) would not indicate knowledge. But it does, so the objection fails.
Although the passage does not explicitly mention God, the implication is clear for divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : ما يمنع من أنه إنما يدل الفعل الحكمي على علم العالم؛ لأنّهُ ممن يجوز أن يموتَ ويَجْهَلَ . قيل له : لو جاز هذا لقائله لجاز لزاعم أن يزعم أنّ الفعلَ الحِكْميَّ يدل على أن العالِمَ عالِم ؛ لأنَّه ممّن يَجُوز أن يموت ويجهل .
If it is said: What prevents that the act of wisdom only indicates the knowledge of the knower because he is one who may die and become ignorant. It is said to him: If this were permissible for its speaker, then it would be permissible for a claimant to claim that the act of wisdom indicates that the knower is a knower because he is one who may die and become ignorant.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector argues that the act of wisdom (الفعل الحكمي) indicates knowledge only because the knower (e.g., a human) is subject to death and ignorance, thus the knowledge is contingent and created. Al-Ash'ari refutes by showing that the same reasoning would then imply that the act indicates that the knower is a knower merely because he can die and become ignorant, which is absurd because the act indicates knowledge, not the knower's epistemic state. The argument is a reductio ad absurdum: if mortality were the basis, it would apply equally to the indication of the knower, but it does not, so the premise is false. Moreover, for God, who does not die, the act of wisdom still indicates His knowledge, proving that mortality is not the reason.

Key Terms
الفعل الحكمي
موت
جهل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The act of wisdom indicates knowledge only because the agent may die and become ignorant.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows that the same reasoning would absurdly also indicate that the agent is a knower due to mortality, which is not the case; therefore, mortality is not the reason the act indicates knowledge.

Checkpoint
How does al-Ash'ari refute the objection that the act indicates knowledge because the knower may die?
A) By asserting that God never dies
B) By showing the same reasoning would absurdly apply to the indication of the knower
C) By denying that humans have real knowledge
D) By claiming the act is not evidence for knowledge

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari refutes objections by showing they lead to absurd conclusions when applied consistently.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you defend your beliefs, do you use reasoning that, if applied consistently to another aspect of your faith, would lead to an absurd conclusion? Take one of your own arguments and test it with al-Ash'ari's mirroring technique.
?
The objector limited God's knowledge based on human mortality. Where in your life do you limit God's attributes based on your own limited experience or circumstances? This lesson demands you align your thinking with divine reality, not your own constraints.
?
Al-Ash'ari refuted an objection by showing its own logic backfires. Are there doubts you entertain about your faith that you have never subjected to the reductio test? Commit to examining one such doubt today using this method.
