العدل
الجور
العجز
الضد

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God is not described as just, He must be unjust or incapable.
Correction: Ash'ari shows that absence of justice does not necessitate its opposite; the same action can be just or unjust based on divine command, and a being can lack justice without being unjust.

Checkpoint
Why does Ash'ari argue that denying God's justice does not imply He is unjust?
A) Because God is above all attributes.
B) Because a person can lack justice without being unjust, and the same action can be just or unjust depending on God's command.
C) Because injustice is impossible for God.
D) Because justice is not an attribute of God.

Key Takeaway
Denying God's justice does not force us to attribute injustice or incapacity to Him, because justice and its opposites are not simple binaries—they depend on divine command.

Refutation of the Claim That God Must Be Either Moving or Still
Ash'ari refutes the objection that if God is not moving, He must be still.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the absence of motion in God does not imply stillness, and how Ash'ari uses logical distinctions and analogy to refute this objection.

Core Idea
Absence of motion does not imply stillness when motion is impossible.

This passage tackles a common objection: if God is not moving, then He must be still. Ash'ari carefully unpacks the meaning of 'moving' and shows that the objector's inference is based on an equivocation. By distinguishing between self-motion and moving another, and by using an analogy with speech, he demonstrates that the conclusion does not follow. Understanding this refutation clarifies how negative attributes (like not being moving) do not automatically entail their opposites in the case of God.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and claim
Start by reading the objector's claim: if God is not moving in eternity, He must be still. Notice the assumption that absence of one attribute implies presence of its opposite.
This is a logical move that Ash'ari will challenge.
2
Identify the two meanings of 'moving'
Ash'ari splits the term 'moving' into two possibilities: moving oneself or moving another. Understand the distinction and how it sets up the refutation.
3
Understand why self-motion is impossible for God
Self-motion would imply change, which is impossible for God. Therefore, the first meaning does not apply, and the objection is invalid in that sense.
This is key to the argument.
4
Examine the analogy with speech
Ash'ari draws an analogy: if someone cannot speak, not speaking does not make them described by silence as an opposite. Similarly, since God cannot move Himself, not moving does not make Him still.
This reinforces the logical fallacy.
5
Reflect on the broader principle
Consider the general principle: absence of a property does not entail its opposite when that property is impossible for the subject. This is crucial in theology to avoid false dichotomies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال : مَا أنكرتُم إذا لم يكنِ البارِي -تعالى- مُحرِّكًا في أزله أن يكونَ مُسَكِّنا ؟ قيل له : لا يخلو قولُكَ : «إذا لم يكن محركًا، أن يكون مسكنا [ مِن أن] تعني : إذا كانَ لم يزلْ غيرَ مُحرِّك لنفسِهِ أن يكونَ مُسَكِّنا لها ، أو تعني إذا لم يكن محركًا لجسم كان مسكنا له . فإن عَنيْتَ : إن لم يحرك نفسَهُ كانَ مسكّنا لها، فهذا خطأ ؛ لأنه يستحيل أن يحرك نفسَهُ ، ونحن لم نقل إذا لم يتكلَّمْ مَنْ يستحيلُ كلامُه كان موصوفا بضد الكلام .
If he says: What prevents you, if the Creator - exalted - is not moving in His eternity, from His being still? It is said to him: Your saying: 'If He is not moving, then He is still' is not free [from being] that you mean: if He has never ceased being non-moving of Himself, that He is still of Himself, or you mean: if He is not moving a body, He is still for it. If you meant: If He does not move Himself, He is still for it, this is wrong; because it is impossible that He moves Himself, and we do not say that if one whose speech is impossible does not speak, he is described by the opposite of speech.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is another objection-and-answer. The objector argues that if God is not 'moving' in eternity, He must be 'still'. The author distinguishes two possible meanings: moving oneself or moving another. If the objector means moving Himself, that is impossible for God (as self-motion implies change). If he means moving a body, the absence of that does not entail stillness in God. The author draws an analogy: if someone cannot speak (due to impossibility), not speaking does not make them described by the opposite (silence) in the same way. Thus, the inference fails.

Key Terms
الحركة
السكون
الضد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Absence of motion must entail presence of stillness.
Correction: This depends on the subject's capacity for motion; if motion is impossible, the opposite does not apply.

Checkpoint
Why does Ash'ari reject the inference that if God is not moving, He must be still?
A) Because God is above all motion.
B) Because the objector confuses self-motion with moving others, and self-motion is impossible for God.
C) Because stillness is not an attribute of God.
D) Because God is always moving in a different sense.

Key Takeaway
The absence of a property in God does not automatically imply its opposite when that property is impossible for Him to possess.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If you truly believe that God is beyond the opposites that define creation, how should that change the way you speak about Him in your daily conversations and in your du'a?

Capacity for Speech Entails Actual Speech
Ashari refutes an objection about capacity for speech using an analogy with knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ashari's argument that a person with capacity for speech necessarily either speaks or is silent, using an analogy with knowledge and its opposites.

Core Idea
Capacity for speech requires actual speech or its opposite — silence cannot coexist with capacity.

This passage presents an objection-and-answer typical of kalam dialectic. An opponent claims that a person capable of speech may be devoid of speech and its opposites. Ashari calls this a contradiction and uses an analogy with knowledge to force the conclusion that the capable person must always have either the act or its opposite.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: objection, initial response, analogy, and conclusion.
The passage ends mid-sentence but the argument is complete.
2
Identify the objection and Ashari's response
The objector claims a capable person can be free from speech and its opposites. Ashari calls this a 'kind of contradiction' and asserts that such a person is necessarily speaking.
3
Analyze the analogy with knowledge
Ashari asks whether the objector would apply the same logic to knowledge. The objector concedes that a person capable of knowledge is free from that specific knowledge and its opposite, but not from all knowledge or its opposite.
This forces the objector to admit that capacity always entails one of two opposites.
4
Apply the analogy to speech
Ashari then demands that the objector say the same about speech: the person capable of speech must always have either speech or its opposite (silence).
5
Reflect on the principle
Understand that Ashari is establishing a general principle: capacity for an act in a living being implies the presence of either the act or its opposite.
This is foundational for arguments about divine attributes later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة فإن قال : القادر منا على الكلام، في حال قدرته عليه ، قد خلا من الكلام وأضداده فهذا ضرب من الخلاف ؛ لأن القادر منا على الكلام، في حال قدرته عليه متكلم لا محالة، وسندل على ذلك بعد هذا الموضع من كتابنا . على أنا نقول له : ما أنكرت أن يكون القادر على العلم، قد خلا من العلم وأضداده؟ فإن قال : القادر على العلم قد خلا من العلم وأضداده، اللذين يقدر عليهما، ولا يخلو من علم آخر أو ضده قيل له : فقل : إن القادر على الكلام وضده اللذين يقدر عليهما
Issue. If he says: The one among us capable of speech, in the state of his capacity for it, is free from speech and its opposites. This is a kind of contradiction; because the one among us capable of speech, in the state of his capacity for it, is necessarily a speaker, and we will demonstrate that later in our book. Moreover, we say to him: Why do you deny that the one capable of knowledge may be free from knowledge and its opposites? If he says: The one capable of knowledge is free from knowledge and its opposites, both of which he is capable, and he is not free from another knowledge or its opposite. It is said to him: Then say: The one capable of speech and its opposite, both of which he is capable.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector claims that a person capable of speech can be devoid of speech and its opposites (i.e., silence). Ashari calls this a contradiction, asserting that a person with capacity for speech is necessarily a speaker. He then uses an analogy: if the objector claims that a person capable of knowledge can be devoid of knowledge and its opposites, he would be forced to admit that such a person still possesses some other knowledge or its opposite. Thus, by analogy, the person capable of speech must always have either speech or its opposite (silence). The answer completes the argument by demanding that the objector apply the same logic to speech.

Key Terms
قادر
كلام
خلو
أضداد
علم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A person with capacity for speech can be silent without any actual speech or its opposite being present.
Correction: Ashari argues that capacity for an act necessarily entails the presence of either the act itself or its opposite; a capable person cannot be in a neutral state.

Checkpoint
What analogy does Ashari use to refute the claim that a person capable of speech may be free from speech and its opposites?
A) The analogy of movement and stillness
B) The analogy of knowledge and its opposites
C) The analogy of life and death
D) The analogy of sight and blindness

Key Takeaway
Ashari shows that capacity for speech necessarily entails either speech or its opposite, using an analogy with knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have the capacity to speak truth, but are you currently exercising that truth, or are you falling into its opposite by remaining silent when you should speak, or by uttering falsehood? There is no neutral state—what will you choose today?
?
If you claim to have the capacity to know Allah, yet you are not actively seeking that knowledge, then according to this lesson, you must be in a state of its opposite (ignorance or distraction). How will you break free from that state and actually pursue knowledge?
?
This lesson exposes the illusion of spiritual neutrality. You cannot say 'I have the ability to do good but I am not doing it now.' Where in your life have you used that excuse, and what concrete step will you take to align your capacity with action?

Proof of the Eternity of God's Speech
Ashari uses a trilemma to prove that God's speech must be eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ash'ari's trilemma argument that God's speech must be eternal, and why the three options for originated speech are impossible.

Core Idea
God's speech is eternal because anything originated cannot be attributed to Him.

This passage presents a classic kalam proof for the eternity of God's attribute of speech. Ash'ari uses a logical trilemma—an exhaustive division of possibilities—to show that speech cannot be created in God's essence, cannot subsist by itself, and cannot be created in another. By eliminating all originated options, he concludes that speech is necessarily eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Ash'ari begins by stating the aim: to prove God has never ceased to be speaking.
2
Identify the three possibilities
The passage presents three ways speech could be originated if it were not eternal: in God's essence, self-subsisting, or in another. Find each one and note how Ash'ari introduces them.
The three possibilities are exhaustive for an originated entity.
3
Examine the impossibilities
For each possibility, Ash'ari gives a reason why it is impossible. Understand each reason: God is not a locus for accidents, an attribute cannot subsist by itself, and a body containing speech would acquire divine qualities.
Focus on the logic: each possibility leads to an unacceptable consequence.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Since all originated possibilities are eliminated, speech must be eternal. Therefore, God has always been speaking. This is a decisive proof in kalam.
This conclusion is a cornerstone of Ash'ari theology on divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودليل آخر على أنَّ الله -تعالى- لم يزل مُتَكلّما : أن الكلام لا يخلو أن يكون قديما أو حديثا : فإن كان مُحدثًا لم يخل أن يحدثه في نفسه، أو قائمًا بنفسه، أو في غيره : فيستحيل أن يحدثه في نفسه؛ لأنه ليسَ بِمَحل للحوادثِ . ويستحيل أن يُحدثه قائما بنفسه؛ لأنَّه صِفَةٌ، والصفةُ لا تقومُ بنفسها . ويستحيل أن يحدثَهُ في غيرِهِ؛ لأنه لو أحدثه في غيره لوجب أن يُشْتَق لذلك الجسمِ الذي فيه الكلام، مِنْ أخص أوصاف الكلام اللازمة له لِنَفْسِهِ : اسمٌ، وللجملة التي المحل منها اسم . فإنْ كان أخصُّ أوصافِ الكلامِ أنَّه كلامٌ ، وجَبَ أنْ يكونَ ذلك الجسم متكلما آمرا . وإن كان أخصُّ أوصافه أنه أمرٌ ، وَجَب أن يكونَ ذلك الجسم آمرا .
Another proof that God—exalted—has never ceased to be speaking: that speech cannot but be either eternal or originated. If it is originated, it cannot but be that He brings it into existence in His essence, or it subsists by itself, or in another. It is impossible for Him to bring it into existence in His essence because He is not a locus for accidents. It is impossible for Him to bring it into existence as subsisting by itself because it is an attribute, and an attribute does not subsist by itself. It is impossible for Him to bring it into existence in another because if He brought it into existence in another, it would be necessary that that body in which the speech is derive a name from the most specific descriptions of speech necessary to it for itself, and for the sentence from which the locus [derives] a name. If the most specific description of speech is that it is speech, then that body must be a speaker, a commander. And if the most specific description of it is that it is a command, then that body must be a commander.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a proof (dalil) for the eternity of God's attribute of speech. The argument is a trilemma (or exhaustive division): speech is either eternal (qadim) or originated (muhdath). If originated, there are three ways it could be brought about: (1) in God's own essence (i.e., as an accident), (2) as a self-subsisting entity, or (3) in another (a created body). Each is shown impossible: (1) because God is not a locus (mahall) for accidents (he is not composed of substance and accident). (2) because speech is a property (sifa) that cannot exist independently. (3) because if speech were in a body, that body would acquire the name from the most specific description of that speech—if the description is 'speech', the body would be called 'speaker'; if 'command', it would be called 'commander'. But it is impossible for a created body to have such divine qualities. Therefore, all originated possibilities are eliminated, so speech must be eternal. Hence God has always been speaking.

Key Terms
قديم
محدث
صفة
محل
متكلما

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that speech could be created in a body without the body becoming a speaker.
Correction: The passage argues that if speech is in a body, that body necessarily derives the name 'speaker' or 'commander' from the most specific description of the speech, which is impossible for a creature.

Checkpoint
Why can't God's speech be created in another (e.g., a body)?
A) Because God cannot create speech in another.
B) Because the other body would then be called 'speaker', which is impossible for a creature.
C) Because speech cannot exist in a body.
D) Because the other body would become eternal.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is eternal because all possible originated scenarios are logically impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's speech is eternal and uncreated, what does that mean for how you approach the Quran? Does your reverence for it match the fact that it is the eternal word of God, not a temporal book?
?
The trilemma shows that any thought of God 'acquiring' speech in time is impossible. Have you ever acted as if God's words or commands were optional or subject to change? How does this proof challenge that assumption in your daily choices?
?
If God is not a locus for accidents, then His attributes are not temporary. How does this affect your certainty in His promises? When you waver in trust, does it stem from an unspoken belief that God might change? What concrete step will you take today to rely on His eternal word?

The Eternity of God's Speech: Proof by Elimination
Imam Ashari argues that God's speech must be eternal by eliminating all possibilities of origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari school argues that God's speech (and therefore the Quran) is eternal, using a proof that eliminates every possible way speech could be originated.

Core Idea
God's speech cannot be originated because every possible locus of origination leads to absurdity.

Imam Ashari presents a crisp logical argument for the eternity of God's speech. He begins by stating that speech is either eternal or originated. He then examines every conceivable way that speech could be originated—in God Himself, standing alone, or in another creature—and shows each to be impossible. The only remaining possibility is that it is eternal, which is the conclusion. This proof is foundational for the Ash'ari doctrine that the Quran is uncreated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Try to follow the flow of the argument before diving into analysis.
2
Identify the three possibilities for originated speech
The passage lists three loci where originated speech could reside: in God, standing by itself, or in another. Identify each and note how the author eliminates them.
These are exhaustive possibilities for any attribute that is originated.
3
Understand why the first two are impossible
The author argues that God cannot be a locus for accidents (originated speech would be an accident), and an attribute cannot exist without a subject. Grasp these foundational principles.
This uses the Ash'ari distinction between substance and accident.
4
Analyze the third possibility
If speech were created in another being, that being would acquire the attributes of speech (speaker, commander, prohibitor). This is absurd because only God is the speaker of His own speech.
This is the most detailed part of the argument.
5
Conclude with the eternity of speech
Since all possibilities of origination are eliminated, speech must be eternal. Reflect on why this proof is important for the doctrine of the Quran.
The Quran is God's speech and therefore eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودليل آخر على أنَّ الله -تعالى- لم يزل مُتَكلّما : أن الكلام لا يخلو أن يكون قديما أو حديثا : فإن كان مُحدثًا لم يخل أن يحدثه في نفسه، أو قائما بنفسه، أو في غيره : فيستحيل أن يحدثه في نفسه؛ لأنه ليس بِمَحل للحوادثِ . ويستحيل أن يُحدثه قائما بنفسه؛ لأنَّه صِفَةٌ، والصفةُ لا تقومُ بنفسها . ويستحيل أن يحدثَهُ في غيرِهِ؛ لأنه لو أحدثه في غيره لوجب أن يُشتق لذلك الجسم الذي فيه الكلام، مِنْ أخص أوصاف الكلام اللازمة له لِنَفْسِهِ : اسمٌ، وللجملة التي المحل منها اسم . فإنْ كان أخصُّ أوصافِ الكلامِ أنَّه كلامٌ ، وجَبَ أنْ يكونَ ذلك الجسم متكلما آمرا . وإن كان أخصُّ أوصافه أنه أمرٌ ، وَجَب أن يكونَ ذلك الجسم آمرا . وكذلك إن كان أخصُّ أوصافِهِ أنَّه نَهْي وجَبَ أنْ يكونَ ذلكَ الجسم ناهيا . فلما اسْتَحالَ أنْ يتكلَّمَ بكَلامِ اللَّهِ -تعالى- غَيْرُه ، ويَأْمُرَ بِأَمْرِهِ غَيْرُهُ ، وينْهَى بِنَهِيهِ غَيْرُهُ، استحالَ أنْ يُحدِثَ كلاما في غيره، فيكون به متكلما . وإذا فسدت الوجوه التي لا يخلو الكلام منها لو كان مُحدَثًا ، صح أنَّه قديمٌ، وأن الله -تعالى- لم يزلْ بِهِ مُتَكلما
Another proof that God - exalted - has never ceased to be speaking: that speech is not free from being eternal or originated. If it is originated, it cannot but be that He originates it in Himself, or standing by itself, or in another. It is impossible that He originates it in Himself because He is not a locus for accidents. It is impossible that He originates it standing by itself because it is an attribute, and an attribute does not subsist by itself. It is impossible that He originates it in another because if He originates it in another, a name would necessarily be derived for that body in which the speech is, from the most specific of the attributes of speech necessary to it for itself, and for the sentence which is the locus a name. If the most specific attribute of speech is that it is speech, then that body must be a speaker, a commander. If the most specific attribute is that it is a command, then that body must be a commander. Likewise, if the most specific attribute is that it is a prohibition, then that body must be a prohibiting entity. So when it is impossible for other than God to speak with God's speech, and for other than Him to command with His command, and for other than Him to prohibit with His prohibition, it is impossible that He originates speech in another so that He would be speaking by it. And when the possibilities from which speech cannot be free if it were originated are invalidated, it is correct that it is eternal, and that God - exalted - has never ceased to be speaking by it.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a proof by elimination. The author argues that God's speech must be eternal because the alternative—that it is originated—leads to impossibilities. He first states the premise: speech is either eternal or originated. If originated, it must be in one of three loci: in God Himself, subsisting by itself, or in something else. Each is shown impossible: God is not a locus for accidents (so speech cannot inhere in Him); an attribute cannot subsist independently (since it requires a subject); and if speech were created in another entity, that entity would acquire the attributes of speech (command, prohibition, etc.) and thus become the speaker, which is absurd because only God is the speaker of His own speech. Therefore, all possibilities of origination are invalid, and speech must be eternal. This is a foundational Ash'ari argument for the uncreatedness of the Quran.

Key Terms
كلام (speech)
قديم (eternal)
محدث (originated)
صفة (attribute)
محل (locus)
متكلم (speaker)
أمر (command)
نهي (prohibition)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God creates speech in a physical object (like the burning bush in the Bible), then God is still the speaker. This argument shows that the object would become the speaker, which is absurd.
Correction: The argument demonstrates that if speech were created in another, that other would be the speaker, not God. So to preserve God's sole speakerhood, speech must be eternal and not created in anything.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is it impossible for God to originate speech in another being?
A) Because God cannot create anything in another.
B) Because that other being would become the speaker, commanding, or prohibiting by that speech.
C) Because speech is not an attribute.
D) Because God only speaks directly without intermediaries.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is eternal because every conceivable way for it to be originated leads to absurdity, such as God being a locus for accidents or a creature becoming the speaker.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly believe you are uttering God’s eternal speech, not a created thing? How does that reality change the way you recite—does it move you to greater awe and submission?
?
If God’s speech is eternal and inseparable from Him, what does it mean for you to hear His commands and prohibitions in the Quran? Are you listening as if God Himself is speaking to you right now, or do you treat it as ancient text?
?
This proof shows that God’s speech cannot be placed in another being. When you hear a human reciter, do you still sense the divine presence in the words? What would it take for you to always hear the Quran as God’s direct address to your soul?

Refutation of the Analogical Objection on Divine Speech
Imam Ashari refutes the Mu'tazilite analogy using reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ashari refutes the Mu'tazilite analogy that God could be a speaker through speech He creates in another, by extending the analogy to show its absurd consequences.

Core Idea
An invalid analogy proves nothing: God's essential attributes cannot be derived from created entities.

The Mu'tazila argued that since God is described as 'actor' and 'favorer' based on acts He originates in creation, He could similarly be 'speaker' through speech He creates in another. Imam Ashari refutes this by extending the analogy: if that were valid, God's knowledge and power would also have to be originated in other things, which is false. This lesson walks through the objection, the counter-argument, and the logical principle that essential divine attributes are eternal, not derived from creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic and translation of the Mu'tazilite objection. Notice the list of divine actions (acts, favors, etc.) that God originates in creation, and the claim that speech should be similar.
The opponent is trying to use God's actions as a model for His speech.
2
Analyze the refutation
Read the refutation. The author says: if the analogy held, then God's knowledge and power would also need to be originated in something else, which is false. So the original analogy fails.
The refutation uses a reductio ad absurdum: the opponent's reasoning leads to an unacceptable conclusion.
3
Identify the key principle
Reflect on why the analogy breaks down. The key is that essential divine attributes (knowledge, power, speech) are eternal and not dependent on created entities, whereas actions like 'creating' and 'giving favor' are relational and do depend on creation.
This distinction is crucial in Islamic theology between eternal attributes and temporal acts.
4
Test your understanding with the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to ensure you grasp the logic of the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالَ : أَفَلَيْسَ قد يُحدِثُ الله - تعالى - في غيره، فعلا وتفضلا ونعمةً وإحسانا ورِزْقًا، فيكون فاعلا متفضلا منعمًا محسنًا رازقا؟ فما أنكرتُمْ أنْ يُحدِثَ في غيره كلاما ، يكون به متكلما ؟ قيل له : لو لزم هذا ، لَلَزِمَ أن يَعلَمَ ويَقدرَ بِعِلم وقُدرةٍ يحدثُهما في غيره، كما يتفضل وينعم ويحسن فيما يحدثه في غيره؛ تفضلا ونعمة وإحسانا ورزقا فإن لم يلزم هذا لم يلزم ما قلتموه .
If he says: 'Does not God - exalted - originate in other than Himself acts, favors, graces, goodness, and sustenance, so He is an actor, a favorer, a gracious one, a good one, a sustainer? So why do you deny that He originates speech in other than Himself, so that He is a speaker by it?' It is said to him: 'If this were necessary, then it would be necessary that He knows and has power by knowledge and power which He originates in other than Himself, just as He favors and gives grace and does good with what He originates in other than Himself, as favor, grace, goodness, and sustenance. So if this is not necessary, then what you say is not necessary.'
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its refutation. The opponent (the Mu'tazila) argues by analogy: God originates acts, favors, and sustenance in created things and is described as an actor, favorer, etc. So why can't He originate speech in something else and be described as a speaker by that speech? The author responds by pointing out that the analogy would also require that God's knowledge and power be originated in other things for Him to be knowing and powerful, which is not the case. Since God is knowing and powerful by eternal attributes (not created in others), the analogy fails. Therefore, the claim that speech can be originated in another is invalid.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's being 'speaker' could be derived from speech He creates in a created entity, just as His being 'actor' comes from acts He creates.
Correction: Essential attributes (knowledge, power, speech) are eternal and not dependent on created entities, whereas relational descriptions like 'actor' refer to God's actions in creation.

Checkpoint
What is the core strategy of Imam Ashari's refutation of the Mu'tazilite objection?
A) He denies that God originates acts in others.
B) He shows that the same reasoning would force God's knowledge and power to be originated in another, which is false.
C) He claims that speech cannot be created at all.
D) He argues that the opponent's question is illogical.

Key Takeaway
Essential divine attributes like speech are eternal and cannot be derived from created entities, unlike relational descriptions like 'actor' which originate from actions in creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Where else in your faith do you draw false comparisons between God and creation? Commit to identifying one such assumption today and replace it with what the Qur'an and Sunnah teach.

When you say 'Allah knows' or 'Allah speaks,' do you truly believe His knowledge and speech are unlike any created knowledge or speech? How does this affect your awe and reverence of Him? Pause now and ask Allah to increase your certainty in His absolute uniqueness.

Proof that God's Speech is Eternal
Ashari concludes that created speech implies another speaker, so speech must be eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ash'ari's conditional proof that God's speech is eternal, and why created speech cannot be attributed to God.

Core Idea
If speech were created, someone else would be the speaker; so God's speech must be eternal.

Imam al-Ash'ari employs a logical argument to establish that God's speech is not created. He considers the implications if speech were created and shows they lead to absurdity. This lesson walks through that reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Let the author's own wording sink in before analyzing.
Notice the conditional structure: 'if... then...'
2
Analyze the conditional reasoning
Follow Ash'ari's logic: if speech were created, it would have specific attributes like being a prohibition. Then ask who would be the speaker if speech resides in another body.
The key point is that the body containing the speech would be the speaker, not God.
3
Conclude with the necessary conclusion
Since all possibilities for created speech lead to contradiction, speech must be eternal. God has never ceased to be a speaker by His eternal speech.
This refutes the view that God's speech is created or that God becomes a speaker temporally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك إن كان أخصُّ أوصافِهِ أنَّه نَهْي وجَبَ أنْ يكونَ ذلكَ الجسم ناهيا . فلما اسْتَحالَ أنْ يتكلَّمَ بكَلامِ اللَّهِ -تعالى- غَيْرُه ، ويَأْمُرَ بِأَمْرِهِ غَيْرُهُ ، وينْهَى بِنَهِيهِ غَيْرُهُ، استحالَ أنْ يُحدِثَ كلاما في غيره، فيكونَ [هو] به متكلما . وإذا فسدت الوجوه التي لا يخلو الكلام منها لو كان مُحدَثًا ، صح أنَّه قديمٌ، وأن الله -تعالى- لم يزلْ بِهِ مُتَكلما
Likewise, if the most specific of its descriptions is that it is a prohibition, then it would be necessary that that body be a prohibitor. When it is impossible that other than God speak with God's speech, and command with His command, and forbid with His prohibition, it is impossible that He create speech in another, so that He becomes a speaker by it. And when the aspects from which speech could not be free if it were created are invalidated, it is correct that it is eternal, and that God - exalted - has never ceased to be a speaker by it.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a conclusive proof that God's speech is eternal. The argument proceeds by conditional reasoning: if speech were created, it would have specific attributes (e.g., if it is a prohibition, the entity in which it resides would be the one prohibiting). But it is impossible for anything other than God to speak with God's speech or command or forbid with His. Therefore, it is impossible that God created speech in another and then become a speaker by that created speech. Since all possible scenarios for created speech lead to absurdity, the only valid conclusion is that God's speech is eternal, and God has always been speaking by it.

قديم
محدث
أخص أوصاف

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God becomes a speaker by creating speech in another entity.
Correction: As Ash'ari argues, if speech were created in another, that entity would be the speaker, not God. Therefore, God's speech cannot be created.

B) God's speech is eternal and not created.
C) Speech is an attribute of bodies.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is eternal because if it were created, it would necessitate another speaker, which is impossible.

Refutation of the Analogy to Created Acts
Ashari refutes the analogy from created acts to speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the analogy between God's creating acts in others and His creating speech in a created object is invalid.

Core Idea
The analogy collapses because it would force an unacceptable consequence.

The Mu'tazilites argued that just as God creates acts in others and is called the doer, He could create speech in a created object and be called the speaker. Imam al-Ashari refutes this by showing that the analogy would lead to an absurdity that even the Mu'tazilites would reject. This passage teaches us how to use logical reasoning to defend divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection carefully: the opponent argues by analogy from God's creating acts in others to His creating speech in another.
The objector is a Mu'tazilite who accepts that God creates acts in others.
2
Identify the refutation strategy
Notice that Ashari does not deny the premise; instead he uses a reductio ad absurdum. He shows that the same logic would force the opponent to accept that God knows and wills by created attributes.
This is a common method in kalam: if the analogy holds, then similar consequences must hold.
3
See why the refutation works
The Mu'tazilites do not accept that God's knowledge and will are created, so they must reject the original analogy. The refutation is decisive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالَ : أَفَلَيْسَ قد يُحدِثُ الله - تعالى - في غيره، فعلا وتفضلا ونعمةً وإحسانا ورِزْقًا، فيكون فاعلا متفضلا منعمًا محسنًا رازقا؟ فما أنكرتُمْ أنْ يُحدِثَ في غيره كلاما ، يكون [هو] به متكلما ؟ قيل له : لو لزِم هذا ، لَلَزِمَ أنْ يعلَمَ ويَقدرَ بِعِلم وقُدرةٍ يحدثُهما في غيره، كما يتفضل وينعم ويحسن فيما يحدثه في غيره؛ تفضلا ونعمة وإحسانا ورزقا فإن لم يلزم هذا لم يلزم ما قلتموه .
If he says: 'Does not God - exalted - create in another, an act, a favor, a blessing, benevolence, and provision, so that He becomes an actor, a bestower of favor, a blesser, a benevolent one, a provider? So why do you deny that He creates speech in another, so that He becomes a speaker by it?' It is said to him: 'If this were necessary, then it would also be necessary that He know and will by knowledge and power that He creates in another, just as He bestows favor and blesses and does good in what He creates in another as favor, blessing, benevolence, and provision. If this is not necessary, then what you said is not necessary.'
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents a classic Mu'tazilite objection and Ashari's response. The objector argues by analogy: God creates acts in other entities (e.g., favor in a person) and is still called the doer, so why can't He create speech in another and be called the speaker? Ashari refutes by showing the analogy leads to an absurdity: if accepted, one would have to also accept that God could know and will by knowledge and power He creates in another. Since Mu'tazilites do not accept that (they affirm God's knowledge and will as eternal), the original analogy fails. The rule is that the conclusion (the analogy to speech) is invalid because it leads to an unacceptable consequence.

فعل

علم
قدرة
قياس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objector believes that because God creates acts in others and is called the doer, He can similarly create speech in another and be called the speaker.
Correction: Ashari shows that this analogy would force the opponent to accept that God's knowledge and will are also created, which they deny, so the analogy is invalid.

Checkpoint
How does Ashari refute the objection that God creates acts in others and is still the doer?
A) He denies that God creates acts in others.
B) He argues that this would also require God to have created knowledge and will, which is impossible.
C) He claims that speech is not an attribute.
D) He says the objector is a heretic.

Key Takeaway
The analogy between God's creating acts in others and His creating speech collapses because it would force the unacceptable conclusion that God's knowledge and will are created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself drawing conclusions about Allah based on human experiences, like the objector did with the analogy? Where in your life might you be making assumptions about His attributes without grounding them in revelation? Commit to reading more about Allah's names and attributes to correct that.
?
The Ashari shows that an argument that seems plausible on the surface can lead to absurdity when fully examined. Think of a belief you hold about Allah or religion that you've never critically examined. Are you willing to test it against the Quran and Sunnah, even if it challenges your comfort? What specific step will you take this week to do that?
?
The objector's reasoning seemed logical but was incomplete. What incomplete or shallow reasoning about your faith have you accepted because it 'sounded right'? Resolve to study the deeper proofs of theology, like this one, to strengthen your conviction.

The Consequence of God Creating Speech in Another
Ashari applies the principle of attribute derivation to refute the analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ashari argues that if God created speech in another being, that being would be called a speaker, making the Mu'tazilite analogy invalid.

Core Idea
If God creates an attribute in something, that thing takes its name.

Ashari continues his refutation of the Mu'tazilites by showing a consequence of their analogy. He points out that when God creates an attribute in an entity, that entity becomes described by that attribute. For example, a body receiving power becomes powerful. Applying this to speech would make the recipient a speaker, which is impossible for anything other than God. This lesson unpacks this argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice how Ashari lists examples of attributes and their recipients.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the principle
Ashari establishes a principle: when God creates an attribute (like power, knowledge, life) in another, that entity is described by the most specific term for that attribute. Find this principle in the text.
Look for the phrase 'أخص أوصاف' (most specific descriptions).
3
Apply the principle to speech
According to the principle, if God created speech in another, that other would be called 'speaker' (a name derived from speech). Understand why Ashari says this is not permissible.
The conclusion is that speech cannot be compared to other created attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في القرآن والإرادة وأيضًا : فإنَّ اللَّهَ -تعالى- إذا أحدث في غيره تفضّلا ونعمةً وفعلا وإحسانا ورِزْقًا، كانَ ذلك الجسم موصوفًا بأخص أوصاف الفعل والتفضلِ والرِّزْقِ والنّعمَةِ والإحسانِ؛ لأنَّهُ إنْ كانَ التفضُلُ والنعمة والإحسان والفعلُ قُوةٌ لا بُدَّ أنْ يكونَ ذلك الجسم قويا . وكذلك إن كانَ عِلمًا أو حياة أو إرادة أو سَمْعًا أو بَصَرًا ، فيجب إذا أحدَثَ كلامًا في غيرِهِ أن يُشْتَقّ [لِذلِكَ] الغيرِ من أوصاف الكلام [اسْم] . فلما لم يجز ذلك ، بطَلَ أنْ يكون الكلامُ مَقِيسًا عَلَى مَا قلتُم مِنْ أن الله - تعالى - يُحدِثُ كلامَهُ في غيره، كما يُحدِثُ فعله وتفضّلَهُ ونِعَمَهُ وإحسانه في غيره .
Chapter on Speech and Will. Also: Verily God - exalted - when He creates in another favor, blessing, act, benevolence, and provision, then that body is described with the most specific descriptions of act, favor, provision, blessing, and benevolence. Because if favor, blessing, benevolence, and act are power, then that body must be powerful. Likewise, if it is knowledge, life, will, hearing, or sight, then it would be necessary, when He creates speech in another, that a name be derived for that other from the descriptions of speech. When that is not permissible, it is invalid that speech be compared to what you said that God creates His speech in another, just as He creates His act, favor, blessings, and benevolence in another.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage provides an additional proof against the Mu'tazilite analogy. It points out that when God creates an attribute in another entity, that entity becomes described by the most specific description of that attribute. For example, if God creates power in a body, that body is called powerful; if He creates knowledge, it is knowledgeable, etc. By the same logic, if God created speech in another entity, that entity would be called a speaker (i.e., the name 'speaker' would be derived from the attribute of speech). Since it is impossible for anything other than God to be a speaker in the divine sense, the analogy breaks down. Therefore, speech cannot be compared to created acts or favors.

Key Takeaway
If God created speech in another being, that being would be called a speaker, which is impossible, so the Mu'tazilite analogy is invalid.

The Objection of Created Writing and Its Answer
Ashari responds to the objection that writing can be created without the substrate becoming a writer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite objection concerning writing and Ashari's initial response distinguishing between necessary and acquired writing.

Core Idea
Writing on a tablet doesn't make it a writer—so why does speech make a speaker?

The Mu'tazilites press an analogy: God creates writing on a tablet, but the tablet is not a writer. So why must the substrate of speech become a speaker? Ashari begins his answer by splitting writing into two types—necessary and acquired—to show the analogy fails.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Notice the objection from the Mu'tazilites.
The objectors use the example of a tablet that receives writing but is not called a writer.
2
Understand the analogy
The analogy is: God creates writing on a tablet, but the tablet is not a writer. Similarly, why should a body that receives God's speech be called a speaker?
This challenges the Ash'ari position that the Qur'an is God's speech subsisting in a non-speaking substrate.
3
Note Ashari's distinction
Ashari distinguishes two types of writing: necessary (directly created by God) and acquired (kasb). He claims that in necessary creation, the substrate becomes a writer by necessity.
The text cuts off before completing the argument for acquired writing.
4
Reflect on the incomplete answer
Consider how the distinction might undermine the objection. If necessary writing makes the substrate a writer, then the analogy fails because the tablet does not have writing created by necessity.
The full argument is not given, but the direction is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : أفليس قد يحدث الله -تعالى- كتابةً في غيره ولا يكون الشيء الذي قامت به الكتابه كاتبا ؟ قيل لهم : إن أحدثَ اللَّهُ -تعالى- في غيرِهِ كتابةٌ ضَرُورَةٌ، كَانَ ذلكَ الغيرُ كاتبا باضطرار، وكذلك إن كانتِ الكتابة كسبا كانَ
If they say: 'Does not God - exalted - create writing in another, and yet the thing in which the writing subsists is not a writer?' It is said to them: 'If God - exalted - creates writing in another by necessity, then that other is a writer by necessity, and likewise if the writing is acquired, it would be...'
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage presents another objection from the Mu'tazilites and the beginning of Ashari's reply. The objectors point out that God creates writing on a tablet or parchment, but we do not call the tablet a 'writer' (it just has writing on it). So why can't God create speech in a body without that body becoming a speaker? Ashari begins his answer by distinguishing two types of writing: (1) writing created necessarily (directly by God), in which case the substrate does become a 'writer' by necessity (i.e., it is properly called a writer in that context); and (2) writing that is acquired (kasb) by a human agent. The text cuts off here, but the argument is likely that the analogy fails because speech is an essential attribute, whereas writing is often accidental, or that in the case of divine action, the substrate does take the name.

Misconception: The writing analogy proves that accidents can subsist without the substrate being the agent.
Correction: Ashari argues that in necessary creation, the substrate does become the agent (writer) by necessity, so the analogy does not hold.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Ashari counters the writing analogy by distinguishing necessary writing (where the substrate becomes a writer) from acquired writing.

The Analogy of Attributes: God's Speech Cannot Inhere in Creation
Ash'ari presents an argument by analogy to refute the creation of God's speech in a substrate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ash'ari argues that if God's speech were created in a substrate, that substrate would have to be described as speaking, which is impossible.

Core Idea
If speech inheres in creation, the creation becomes a speaker—and that is impossible.

In this passage, Imam al-Ash'ari presents a powerful analogy to refute the claim that God's speech is created in a substrate. He shows that just as the presence of strength makes a body strong, and knowledge makes it knowing, the presence of speech would make the substrate a speaker. Since a created thing cannot be described as speaking with the eternal speech of Allah, the claim fails.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation slowly. Notice how the argument proceeds from a general principle to a specific conclusion.
The Arabic has some OCR issues; the meaning is clear from the translation.
2
Identify the analogies
Find where al-Ash'ari lists attributes like strength, knowledge, life, etc. that God creates in a substrate, and how the substrate is then described.
These analogies set up the expectation for how speech would work.
3
Understand the conclusion
Trace why al-Ash'ari says the analogy fails for speech: because the substrate would be called 'speaking', which is impossible for a created thing.
This conclusion refutes the opponent's claim.
4
Connect to the broader argument
Reflect on how this argument supports the eternity of the Quran, as God's speech cannot be created in a temporal substrate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضًا : فإنَّ اللَّهَ -تعالى- إذا أحدث في غيره تفضّلا ونعمةً وفعلا وإحسانا ورِزْقًا، كانَ ذلك الجسم موصوفًا بأخص أوصاف الفعل والتفضلِ والرِّزْقِ والنّعمَةِ والإحسانِ؛ لأنَّهُ إنْ كانَ التفضُلُ والنعمة والإحسان والفعلُ قُوةٌ لا بُدَّ أنْ يكونَ ذلك الجسم قويا . وكذلك إن كانَ عِلمًا أو حياة أو إرادة أو سَمْعًا أو بَصَرًا ، فيجـ إذا أحدَثَ كلامًا في غيرِهِ أن يُشْتَقَ [لِذلِكَ] الغيرِ من أوصاف الكلامِ [اسْمٌ] . أخَصٌ فلما لم يُجز ذلك ، بطَلَ أنْ يكون الكلامُ مَقِيسًا عَلَى مَا قلتُم مِنْ أن الله - تعالى - يُحدِثُ كلامَهُ في غيره، كما يُحدِثُ فعله وتفضّلَهُ ونِعَمَهُ وإحسانه في غيره . فإن قالوا : أفليس قد يحدث الله -تعالى- كتابةً في غيره ولا يكون الشيء الذي قامت به الكتابه كاتبا ؟ قيل لهم : إن أحدثَ اللَّهُ -تعالى- في غيرِهِ كتابةٌ ضَرُورَةٌ، كَانَ ذلكَ الغيرُ كاتبا باضطرار، وكذلك إن كانتِ الكتابة كسبا كانَ ذلك الغير كاتبا باكتساب، فيجب إذا أحدثَ اللَّهُ - تعالى - كلامَهُ في غيره، أنْ يكونَ ذلكَ الغيرُ مُتكلّما بكلام الله
And also: Verily Allah—exalted is He—when He creates in another favor, grace, act, beneficence, and provision, that body is described with the most specific descriptions of the act, favor, provision, grace, and beneficence; because if the favor, grace, beneficence, and act are strength, then necessarily that body is strong. Similarly, if it is knowledge, life, will, hearing, or sight, then when He creates speech in another, that other should derive a name from the descriptions of speech. [Most specific.] So when that is not permissible, it becomes invalid that speech be analogized to what you said—that Allah—exalted is He—creates His speech in another, just as He creates His act, favor, graces, and beneficence in another. If they say: 'Does not Allah—exalted is He—create writing in another, and the thing in which writing inheres is not a writer?' It is said to them: If Allah—exalted is He—creates writing in another by necessity, then that other is a writer by necessity; and similarly, if the writing is acquired, then that other is a writer by acquisition. So it is necessary, if Allah—exalted is He—creates His speech in another, that that other be one who speaks with the speech of Allah.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that Allah's speech is created in a substrate. The argument proceeds by analogy: When Allah creates an attribute like favor, strength, knowledge, etc. in a body, that body is described with its most specific descriptor (e.g., strong, knowing). Therefore, if Allah created speech in another, that other would have to be described as 'speaking' with that speech. But this is impossible because it would mean a created thing speaks with the eternal speech of Allah. The opponents object by citing the case of writing: Allah creates writing in a thing without that thing becoming a writer. Al-Ash'ari answers that if the writing is necessitated, the thing is a writer by necessity; if acquired, by acquisition. Similarly, if speech were created, the substrate would be a speaker. Since it is not permissible for a created thing to be described as speaking with Allah's speech, the analogy fails, and Allah's speech must be eternal, not created in a substrate.

Correction: Al-Ash'ari argues that if speech inhered in a created thing, that thing would be described as speaking, which is impossible for a created thing with respect to Allah's eternal speech.

A) The substrate would be described as speaking.
B) The substrate would become strong.
C) The substrate would become knowledgeable.
D) The substrate would remain unchanged.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari demonstrates that if speech inhered in a created thing, that thing would be a speaker, which is impossible, thus speech must be eternal.

The Writing Analogy: Answering the Objection
Ash'ari answers an objection using the case of writing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari refutes the objection that God can create writing in a substrate without the substrate becoming a writer, thus undermining the analogy.

Core Idea
Writing does not create a writer without acquisition, but speech would necessitate a speaker.

In this continuation, al-Ash'ari addresses an objection: opponents argue that God creates writing in a thing without that thing becoming a writer, so why can't He create speech in a thing without it becoming a speaker? Al-Ash'ari responds by distinguishing between necessitated and acquired writing, and shows that the analogy actually supports his position.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and Ash'ari's response
Read the passage from 'فإن قالوا' to the end. Notice the structure: an objection is raised, then answered.
2
Understand the two cases of writing
Al-Ash'ari divides writing into two types: by necessity (directly from Allah) and by acquisition (kasb). In both cases, the substrate is called a writer.
This shows that writing does not escape the rule.
3
Apply the same logic to speech
If writing makes the substrate a writer, then speech would make the substrate a speaker. Thus the objection backfires.
4
Conclude the refutation
Understand that Ash'ari's response strengthens his original argument: the analogy from writing actually supports his position.

Proof for the Pre-Eternity of Divine Will
Ash'ari proves that God's will is eternal via impossibility of its creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ash'ari argued that God's will must be eternal by eliminating all possibilities of its temporal creation.

Core Idea
God's will cannot be created because no possible substrate for its creation is coherent.

This passage presents a parallel argument to the one for divine speech. Ash'ari shows that if will were temporal, it would have to exist in some way—as a self-subsisting attribute, created in God's essence, or created in another. Each possibility is impossible. By process of elimination, will must be eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument sink in before analyzing.
Notice the parallel structure with the proof for speech.
2
Identify the three possibilities
The passage presents three options for how a created will could exist. Find each one in the text.
They are: in His essence, in another, or self-subsisting.
3
Understand why each is impossible
For each possibility, Ash'ari gives a reason: (1) God's essence is not a locus for events, (2) an attribute cannot subsist by itself, (3) creating in another would make that other willing by God's will. Grasp each reasoning.
The proof depends on the impossibility of these three.
4
Connect to the conclusion
Since all possibilities are exhausted and impossible, the only remaining conclusion is that will is eternal. Trace the logic from impossibility to necessity.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
5
Reflect on the parallel with speech
The passage opens by stating that this proof is the same as for speech. Compare the reasoning for both attributes to see the consistent method.
This shows a systematic approach in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدم الإرادة وهذا الدليل على قدم الكلام، هو الدليل على قدم الإرادةِ للَّهِ - تعالى ؛ لأنَّها لو كانتْ مُحدَثة لكانت لا تخلُو مِنْ : أن يكونَ يُحدِثها في نفْسِهِ، أو في غيره، أو قائمة بنفسها . فيستحيل أن يُحدثها في نفسه؛ لأنه ليسَ بِمحل للحوادث. ويستحيلُ أن يُحدثَها قائمةً بنفسها ؛ لأنها صفةٌ ، والصِّفةُ لا تقومُ بنفسها، كما لا يجوز أن يُحدِثَ علمًا وقدرة قائمين بأنفسهما . ويستحيل أن يُحدِثَها في غير ؛ لأنَّ هذا يُوجِبُ أنْ يكونَ ذلك الغير مريدًا بإرادةِ اللَّهِ -تعالى-. فلما استحالت هذه الوجوه التي لا تخلو الإرادة منها ، لو كانت محدثة، صَحَّ أنَّها قديمةٌ، وأنَّ اللَّهَ لم يَزِلْ مُرِيدًا بِها .
The pre-eternity of will. And this proof for the pre-eternity of speech is the proof for the pre-eternity of will for Allah—exalted is He—because if it were created, it would not be free from: He creates it in Himself, or in another, or it subsists by itself. It is impossible for Him to create it in Himself, because He is not a locus for events. And it is impossible for Him to create it subsisting by itself, because it is an attribute, and an attribute does not subsist by itself, just as it is not permissible for Him to create knowledge and power subsisting by themselves. And it is impossible for Him to create it in another, because this would necessitate that other be willing by the will of Allah—exalted is He. So when these possibilities, from which will would not be free if it were created, are impossible, it is established that it is eternal, and that Allah has never ceased to be willing with it.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the pre-eternity (قدم) of the divine attribute of will (إرادة). The proof is parallel to the earlier proof for speech. The author presents a trilemma: if God's will were created (محدثة), it must be either (1) created in His essence, (2) created in another, or (3) created as self-subsisting. Each is impossible. First, God's essence cannot be a locus for temporal events (محل للحوادث). Second, an attribute cannot subsist by itself; it must inhere in a subject—knowledge and power cannot exist independently. Third, if it were created in another, that other would be described as willing by God's will, which is absurd (a creature cannot be said to will with God's eternal will). Since all options are impossible, the will must be eternal, meaning God has always been willing with it.

Key Terms
إرادة
قدم
محدثة
صفة
قائمة بنفسها
محل للحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's will could be created in time, like human will.
Correction: Temporal creation requires a substrate for the attribute to inhere in; but God's essence cannot be a locus of events, an attribute cannot be self-subsisting, and creating in another would make that creature a co-willer. All are impossible, so will must be eternal.

Checkpoint
What are the three impossible scenarios if God's will were created, according to al-Ash'ari?
A) In God's essence, in another, or self-subsisting.
B) In God's essence, in heaven, or on earth.
C) By God, by angels, or by prophets.
D) As speech, as power, or as knowledge.

Key Takeaway
God's will is eternal because all conceivable modes of its temporal creation are impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof shows that God's will cannot change because it is eternal. Consider a recent moment when you wished God's plan would change to suit your desires. How can you learn to entrust your specific, time-bound hopes to a will that does not change?
?
If God's will is eternal and never created, then every event that happens was never a 'new decision' for God. Does this change how you think about your daily prayers? Do you pray expecting God to 'decide' something new, or to actualize what He has eternally willed?
?
The proof eliminates the possibility that God's will could be created in another being. This means no creature can ever be a genuine agent of divine will. How does this affect your view of your own ability to do good? Are you truly acting with His will, or only acting within it?

Proof that the Divine Will is Eternal
Al-Ash'ari argues for the eternity of God's will using exhaustive division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari uses a reductio ad absurdum argument to prove that God's will is eternal, not created.

Core Idea
God's will is eternal because creation requires a locus, which God cannot be.

Al-Ash'ari now applies the same logical method he used for speech to prove that God's will is also eternal. He considers all possible ways a created will could exist and demonstrates each is impossible, thus establishing its eternity. This passage illustrates the kalam method of exhaustive division (taqsīm) and elimination.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the parallel with the earlier proof for the eternity of speech.
2
Identify the three possibilities
The passage presents three possible ways a created will could exist. Identify each one and see how the author formulates them.
These are: in God's essence, as an independent substance, or in another being.
3
Understand the refutation of each
For each possibility, Al-Ash'ari gives a reason why it is impossible. Notice the principles behind each refutation: God is not a locus for temporal events; attributes do not subsist by themselves; a will in another would make that other a willer by God's will.
These principles are foundational in Kalam.
4
Conclude the argument
Since all three possibilities are impossible, the will cannot be created. Therefore it must be eternal, and God has always been willing by it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدم الإرادة وهذا الدليل على قدم الكلام، هو الدليل على قدم الإرادةِ للَّهِ - تعالى ؛ لأنَّها لو كانتْ مُحدَثة لكانت لا تخلُو مِنْ : أن يكونَ يُحدِثها في نفْسِهِ، أو في غيره، أو قائمة بنفسها . فيستحيل أن يُحدثها في نفسه؛ لأنه ليسَ بِمحل للحوادث. ويستحيلُ أن يُحدثَها قائمةً بنفسها ؛ لأنها صفةٌ ، والصِّفةُ لا تقومُ بنفسها، كما لا يجوز أن يُحدِثَ علمًا وقدرة قائمين بأنفسهما . ويستحيل أن يُحدِثَها في غير ؛ لأنَّ هذا يُوجِبُ أنْ يكونَ ذلك الغير مريدًا بإرادةِ اللَّهِ -تعالى-. فلما استحالت هذه الوجوه التي لا تخلو الإرادة منها ، لو كانت محدثة، صَحَّ أنَّها قديمةٌ، وأنَّ اللَّهَ لم يَزَلْ مُرِيدًا بِها .
The proof for the eternity of the will: This proof for the eternity of speech is also the proof for the eternity of the will of Allah, Exalted is He. Because if the will were created, it would not be free from being: either He creates it in His own essence, or in another, or it is subsistent by itself. It is impossible that He creates it in His own essence because He is not a locus for temporal events. And it is impossible that He creates it as subsistent by itself because it is an attribute, and the attribute does not subsist by itself, just as it is not permissible that He should create knowledge and power as subsistent by themselves. And it is impossible that He creates it in another because this requires that that other be a willer by the will of Allah, Exalted is He. So when these possibilities, from which the will would not be free if it were created, are impossible, it is established that it is eternal and that Allah has never ceased to be a willer by it.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage presents a proof (dalil) for the eternity (qidam) of the divine will (al-irada). Imam al-Ash'ari uses the same method he used earlier for the divine speech (kalam). The argument is a reductio ad absurdum: If the will were created (muhdatha), then it would have to exist in one of three ways: either in God's own essence, or in another being, or as an independent substance. Each possibility is shown to be impossible. First, it cannot be in God's essence because God is not a locus (mahall) for temporal events (hawadith). Second, it cannot be an independent substance because it is an attribute (sifa) and attributes do not subsist by themselves. Third, it cannot be in another being because that being would then be described as willing by God's will, which is absurd. Since all three possibilities are eliminated, the will must be eternal (qadima) and God has always been willing (murid) by it.

Key Terms
إرادة (irada)
قدم (qidam)
محدث (muhdath)
صفة (sifa)
محل للحوادث (mahall lil-hawadith)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's attributes like will are created in time.
Correction: This proof shows they are eternal because creation requires a subject, which is impossible for God.

Checkpoint
What is the third impossibility that al-Ash'ari mentions regarding a created will?
A) It cannot be created in God's essence.
B) It cannot be created as an independent substance.
C) It cannot be created in another being.
D) It cannot be created at all.

Key Takeaway
God's will is eternal because none of the possible ways for it to be created are tenable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that God's will is eternal and never changes, does your heart find rest in knowing that His decree for you was settled before time began, or do you sometimes wish His will could change to suit your desires? What does your reaction reveal about your trust in His wisdom?
?
If God's will cannot be created in another because that would make that being a 'willer by God's will', how does this affect your understanding of human free will? Do you ever act as if your choices are independent of God's eternal will, and how does this passage call you to align your will with His?
?
The proof shows that God's attributes are not like created things—they are eternal and inherent to His essence. Are there areas in your life where you treat God's commands or attributes as if they were temporary or negotiable? What would change if you fully internalized that His will is as eternal and unchanging as He is?

God's Will Encompasses All Created Things
Al-Ash'ari argues that God's will is universal, using analogy to knowledge and creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the twofold argument by which al-Ash'ari establishes that God's will is universal, encompassing everything that can be willed, and how this follows from it being an attribute of the essence.

Core Idea
God's will, like His knowledge, must cover everything possible because it is essential to Him.

This lesson opens a new chapter on the divine will. Al-Ash'ari anticipates a common objection: why believe God wills everything? He responds with two tightly linked arguments—one from the nature of essential attributes, and another from the act of creation, capped with a Qur'anic verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the chapter opening and objection
Notice how al-Ash'ari sets up the discussion with a question: 'Why do you say that Allah wills everything that can be willed?' This frames the entire argument.
The objection is a standard dialectical device in kalam.
2
Understand the first proof from essential attributes
The will is an attribute of the essence (sifat al-dhat), just like knowledge. As knowledge must encompass all knowable things, so will must encompass all willable things.
This is an argument by analogy, using a previously established principle.
3
Examine the second proof from creation
God is the creator of every temporal thing. It is impossible that He creates something without willing it. Therefore, His will covers all created things.
This proof connects will to creative action.
4
Reflect on the Qur'anic support
The verse 'Doer of what He wills' (Hud 11:107) directly confirms that God does whatever He wills, implying His will is universal.
The verse serves as scriptural evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في الإرادة وأنها تعم سائر المُحدَثاتِ. فإن قال قائل : لم قلتُم : إِنَّ اللَّهَ - تعالى - مُرِيدٌ لكلِّ شيءٍ يَجوزُ أن يُراد؟ قيل له : قُلنا ذلك؛ لأن الإرادة إذا كانت من صفات الذات، بالدلالة التي ذكرناها، وجب أن تكون عامة، في كلِّ ما يجوز أن يُراد على حقيقته، كما إذا كان العلم من صفات الذات وجب عمومه بكلِّ ما يجوز أن يُعلم على حقيقته. وأيضًا فقد دلت الدلالة على أن الله - تعالى - خالق كل شيء حادث، ولا يجوز أن يخلق ما لا يريده، وقد قال الله -تعالى-: {فَعَّالٌ لِمَا يُرِيدُ} [هود: 107].
Chapter: Discussion on the Will and that it encompasses all created things. If a questioner says: Why do you say that Allah, Exalted is He, is a willer of everything that can be willed? It is said to him: We said that because when the will is from the attributes of the essence, by the evidence we have mentioned, it is necessary that it be general, concerning everything that can be willed in reality, just as when knowledge is from the attributes of the essence, its generality is necessary concerning everything that can be known in reality. And also the evidence has indicated that Allah, Exalted is He, is the creator of every created thing, and it is not permissible that He creates what He does not will, and Allah, Exalted is He, has said: 'Doer of what He wills' (Hud 11:107).
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter (bab) on the divine will (al-irada), specifically that it encompasses (ta'ummu) all created things (al-muhdathat). The chapter opens with an objection (fa'in qala qa'il) and its answer. The objector asks: Why do you claim that God is willing (murid) of everything that can possibly be willed? The answer is twofold. First, since the will is an attribute of the essence (sifat al-dhat), as proven earlier (presumably in the previous argument for its eternity), it must be universal in scope, just like divine knowledge ('ilm) which is an attribute of the essence and applies to everything knowable. Second, there is a proof from creation: God is the creator (khaliq) of every temporal thing (hadith), and it is impossible that He creates something He does not will. This is supported by the Qur'anic verse 'Doer of what He wills' (Fa''alun lima yurid). Thus, the will must encompass all things that occur.

Key Terms
إرادة
صفات الذات
عموم
علم
خالق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God does not will evil or certain temporal events, or that His will is limited to good only.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari clarifies that God's will is universal: He wills everything that occurs, including what appears evil, but this is based on His wisdom. The passage asserts that God is the creator of everything temporal and must will it.

Checkpoint

B) The universality of God's knowledge

Key Takeaway
God's will, as an essential attribute, necessarily encompasses all things that can be willed, just as His knowledge encompasses all knowable things.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does Al-Ash'ari's argument that God's will encompasses all created things—including that event—challenge your resistance? What would change if you truly believed that God willed everything that happens, even the painful parts?
?
The passage says that God is 'Doer of what He wills.' Think of a habit or sin you struggle with. If God wills everything that occurs, does that mean He wills your struggle? How does the fact that His will is based on infinite wisdom—not blind fate—allow you to trust Him while still striving to change? What step can you take today to surrender that struggle to His will?
?
Consider the analogy between God's knowledge and His will. You likely trust that God knows everything about you. But do you trust that He wills everything about you—your strengths, weaknesses, circumstances? What would it look like to live today with the conviction that God's will for you is as comprehensive as His knowledge? Name one specific area of your life where you will consciously affirm 'God wills this for me' before the day ends.
